Pāśupata Sūtra - Comprehensive Scholarly Analysis

Sentence-by-Sentence Translation with Linguistic Analysis

Sanskrit Text Word-by-Word Analysis Literal Translation Interpretative Meaning Literary Translation
OPENING INVOCATION - MAṄGALA VERSES
hitārtham akhilam yena
brahmādikam jagat sṛṣṭam
praṇamya tam paśupatim
śirasā sadasatpatim		 • hita-artham = for the sake of welfare/salvation (acc. sg. n.)
• akhilam = whole, entire (nom. sg. n.)
• yena = by whom (instr. sg. m.)
• brahma-ādikam = beginning with Brahmā (nom. sg. n.)
• jagat = world, universe (nom. sg. n.)
• sṛṣṭam = created, emitted (nom. sg. n. PPP from √sṛj)
• praṇamya = having bowed (abs. from pra-√nam)
• tam = that, him (acc. sg. m.)
• paśu-patim = Lord of Souls (acc. sg. m.)
• śirasā = with the head (instr. sg. n.)
• sat-asat-patim = Lord of existent and nonexistent (acc. sg. m.) 		For the sake of (artham) welfare (hita), the whole (akhilam) world (jagat) beginning with (ādikam) Brahmā (brahma) [was] created (sṛṣṭam) by whom (yena), having bowed (praṇamya) to that (tam) Lord of Souls (paśupatim) with the head (śirasā), [the] Lord (patim) of existent (sat) [and] nonexistent (asat)... Opening invocatory sentence. Absolutive praṇamya = reverential gesture completed before main action. Instrumental śirasā = prostration with head (highest respect). Paśu-pati = "Lord of bound souls/animals" (technical term). Sat-asat-pati = Lord of manifest (sat) and unmanifest (asat) realities. Relative clause yena...sṛṣṭam describes Paśupati as cosmic creator. Compound hita-artha = "welfare-purpose" (soteriological aim). Brahma-ādika = "Brahmā-and-so-on" (the entire hierarchy from highest deity down). PPP sṛṣṭa from √sṛj = divine creative act of emission/projection. Having bowed my head to that Lord of existent and nonexistent, Lord of Souls (Paśupati), by whom the whole world has been emitted from Brahmā down, for the sake of (our) salvation...
arthātiśayasaṃpannam
jñānātiśayam uttamam
pañcārtham saṃpravakṣyāmi
yathāvad anupūrvaśaḥ		 • artha-atiśaya-saṃpannam = imbued with superior significance (acc. sg. n.)
• jñāna-atiśayam = superior in knowledge (acc. sg. n.)
• uttamam = most excellent, supreme (acc. sg. n.)
• pañca-artham = the Five Realities (acc. sg. n.)
• saṃpravakṣyāmi = I will teach (1st sg. fut. from sam-pra-√vac)
• yathā-vat = duly, according to truth (adv.)
• anupūrvaśaḥ = in proper order, sequentially (adv.) 		[Which is] imbued with (saṃpannam) superior (atiśaya) significance (artha), superior (atiśaya) in knowledge (jñāna), [and] most excellent (uttamam), the Five Realities (pañcārtham) I will teach (saṃpravakṣyāmi) duly (yathāvat), in proper order (anupūrvaśaḥ). Main declarative statement with compound object. Main verb: saṃpravakṣyāmi (future tense = authorial intention). Pañca-artha = technical term for the five ontological categories (kārya, kāraṇa, yoga, vidhi, duḥkhānta). Three qualifications of the teaching: artha-atiśaya-saṃpanna = "filled/endowed with (saṃpanna) surpassing (atiśaya) meaning/significance"; jñāna-atiśaya = extraordinary in knowledge content; uttama = superlative - highest among teachings. Yathāvat = "according to reality/truth" (accurate transmission). Anupūrvaśas = "in sequence without skipping" (systematic pedagogy). I will duly teach, in good order and adhering to the truth, 'The Five Realities' (Pañcārtha), which is imbued with superior significance, is superior in knowledge, and most excellent.
Full Translation of Opening Verses:

"Having bowed my head to that Lord of existent and nonexistent, Lord of Souls (Paśupati), by whom the whole world has been emitted from Brahmā down, for the sake of (our) salvation, I will duly teach, in good order and adhering to the truth, 'The Five Realities' (Pañcārtha), which is imbued with superior significance, is superior in knowledge, and most excellent."
PRESENTATION OF THE CATEGORIES - PUPIL'S QUESTION
āha: vakṣyati bhagavān pañcārtham • āha = [the pupil] said (3rd sg. perf. from √ah)
• vakṣyati = will teach (3rd sg. fut. from √vac)
• bhagavān = His Lordship, the Lord (nom. sg. m.)
• pañca-artham = the Five Realities (acc. sg. n.) 		[The pupil] said (āha): 'His Lordship (bhagavān) will teach (vakṣyati) [the system of] the Five Realities (pañcārtham)... Dialogue marker āha introduces pupil's voice. Perfect tense = narrative device. Bhagavān = respectful address (lit. "possessing fortune/lordship"). Future vakṣyati shows anticipation of systematic teaching. Pupil (āha): 'His Lordship (bhagavān) will teach (the system) of the five realities (pañcārtha)...
athāsyādisūtram kim iti • atha = well then, now (particle)
• asya = of this/its (gen. sg. n.)
• ādi-sūtram = first sūtra (nom. sg. n.)
• kim = what? (nom. sg. n. interr.)
• iti = thus (quotative) 		Well then (atha), what (kim) [is] its (asya) first (ādi) sūtra (sūtram)? Pupil's question seeking the opening sūtra. Atha = transitional particle marking new inquiry. Compound ādi-sūtra = "beginning-aphorism". Interrogative kim requests identification. Iti marks end of quotation. well then, which is its first Sūtra?'
atrocyate: • atra = here, in this case (adv.)
• ucyate = it is said (3rd sg. pres. pass. from √vac) 		Here (atra) it is said (ucyate): Commentator's formula introducing authoritative answer. Passive ucyate = impersonal construction (scriptural voice). Atra = "in this matter/context". Here it is said:
PĀŚUPATA SŪTRA 1.1 - THE OPENING APHORISM
athātaḥ paśupateḥ pāśupataṃ yogavidhim vyākhyāsyāmaḥ • atha = certainly, now (particle)
• ataḥ = therefore, because of this (particle)
• paśu-pateḥ = of Paśupati, Lord of Souls (gen. sg. m.)
• pāśupatam = Pāśupata, relating to Paśupati (acc. sg. n.)
• yoga-vidhim = praxis/method of union (acc. sg. m.)
• vi-ā-khy-āsy-āmaḥ = we shall explain (1st pl. fut. from vi-ā-√khyā) 		Certainly (atha), therefore (ataḥ), [regarding] Paśupati (paśupateḥ), we shall explain (vyākhyāsyāmaḥ) the Pāśupata (pāśupatam) praxis (vidhim) of union (yoga). The foundational sūtra. Two particles (atha/ataḥ) establish authority and causality. Genitive paśupateḥ = genitive of reference/relation. Pāśupata = taddhita derivative (that which pertains to/is proclaimed by Paśupati). Yoga-vidhi = compound "union-method" (systematic practice). Future vyākhyāsyāmaḥ = commitment to exposition. Certainly, therefore, of Paśupati, we shall explain the Pāśupata praxis of union.
Full Translation of PS 1.1:

"Certainly, therefore, of Paśupati, we shall explain the Pāśupata praxis of union."
KAUṆḌINYA'S COMMENTARY - WORD DIVISION
etat prathamasūtram śāstrādāv uccāryate • etat = this (nom. sg. n.)
• prathama-sūtram = first sūtra (nom. sg. n.)
• śāstra-ādau = at the beginning of the śāstra (loc. sg. m.)
• uccāryate = is spoken (3rd sg. pres. pass. from ud-√car) 		This (etat) first (prathama) sūtra (sūtram) is spoken (uccāryate) at the beginning (ādau) of the śāstra (śāstra). Establishes textual location. Demonstrative etat points to PS 1.1. Compound śāstra-āda = "beginning of the teaching". Passive uccāryate = traditional recitation/pronunciation. This first Sūtra is spoken at the beginning of the Śāstra.
tadanantaram padavigr ahaḥ kriyate • tat-anantaram = immediately after that (adv.)
• pada-vigrahaḥ = word-division, analysis (nom. sg. m.)
• kriyate = is made (3rd sg. pres. pass. from √kṛ) 		Immediately (anantaram) after that (tat), a division (vigrahaḥ) of words (pada) is made (kriyate). Methodological statement. Compound pada-vigraha = "word-separation/analysis" (grammatical procedure). Tadanantaram = temporal sequence. Passive kriyate = standard commentarial practice. Next a division is made of the words.
aṣṭapadam sūtram • aṣṭa-padam = eight-worded (nom. sg. n.)
• sūtram = the sūtra (nom. sg. n.) 		The sūtra (sūtram) [consists of] eight (aṣṭa) words (padam). Numerical analysis. Bahuvṛḥi compound aṣṭa-pada = "having eight words/padas". Establishes precise count for grammatical parsing. The Sūtra counts eight words.
tatra athāta iti dve pade naipātike • tatra = therein, among these (adv.)
• atha-ataḥ = atha and ataḥ (indecl.)
• iti = thus
• dve = two (nom. dual n.)
• pade = words (nom. dual n.)
• naipātike = particles (nom. dual n.) 		Therein (tatra), the two (dve) words (pade) 'atha' (certainly) and 'ataḥ' (therefore) [are] particles (naipātike). Grammatical classification. Naipātika = indeclinable particles (from nipāta). Dual number (dve pade) for the two function words. These establish logical framework (certainty + causation) without inflectional meaning. The two words atha ('certainly') and ataḥ ('because of') are particles (nipāta).
paśupater ity etat padam parigraha arthonocc āryate • paśu-pateḥ = of Paśupati (gen. sg.)
• iti = thus
• etat = this (nom. sg. n.)
• padam = word (nom. sg. n.)
• parigraha-arthena = for the purpose of acceptance/inclusion (instr. sg. m.)
• uccāryate = is spoken (3rd sg. pres. pass.) 		This (etat) word (padam) 'paśupateḥ' (of Paśupati) is spoken (uccāryate) for the purpose (arthena) of acceptance (parigraha). Functional analysis. Parigraha-artha = "purpose of taking up/embracing" - indicates acceptance/adoption of Paśupati's teaching. Genitive case shows relation/reference to the divine source. Paśupater ('of Paśupati'), this word is spoken to indicate acceptance (parigraha).
pāśupatam iti taddhitam • pāśupatam = Pāśupata (nom. sg. n.)
• iti = thus
• taddhitam = nominal derivative (nom. sg. n.) 		'Pāśupatam' (pāśupatam) [is] a nominal derivative (taddhitam). Morphological classification. Taddhita = secondary nominal suffix (Pāṇinian term for derived nominals). Formed from paśu-pati + suffix -a, meaning "that which relates to/belongs to Paśupati." 'Pāśupata' is a nominal derivative (taddhita).
yogavidhim iti sāmāsikam • yoga-vidhim = praxis of union (acc. sg. m.)
• iti = thus
• sāmāsikam = compound (nom. sg. n.) 		'Yogavidhim' (yogavidhim) (praxis of union) [is] a compound (sāmāsikam). Identifies tatpuruṣa compound. Sāmāsika = compound formation. Yoga-vidhi = "union-method/procedure" (karmadhāraya or tatpuruṣa type). 'Praxis of union' is a compound (samāsa).
vi ā iti dve pade • vi = prefix vi- (separate)
• ā = prefix ā- (toward)
• iti = thus
• dve = two (nom. dual n.)
• pade = words (nom. dual n.) 		Vi and ā [in vyākhyāsyāmaḥ] [are] two (dve) words (pade). Prefix analysis. Treats verbal prefixes (upasargas) as separate countable units. Vi = "apart, distinctly"; ā = "toward, thoroughly". Together modify root √khyā "to tell." Vi and ā (in vyākhyāsyāmaḥ) are two words.
khyāsyāma ity ākhyātikam • khyāsyāmaḥ = we shall tell/explain (1st pl. fut.)
• iti = thus
• ākhyātikam = verbal form, finite verb (nom. sg. n.) 		Khyāsyāmaḥ [is] the verb (ākhyātikam). Identifies the finite verbal element (ākhyāta). Root √khyā + future tense + 1st person plural = vyākhyāsyāmaḥ "we shall explain fully." Khyāsyāmaḥ is the verb.
PURPOSE OF WORD DIVISION (PADAVIGRAHA)
āha: kim prayojanam padavigrahaḥ kriyate • āha = [pupil] said (3rd sg. perf.)
• kim = what? (nom. sg. n.)
• prayojanam = purpose (nom. sg. n.)
• pada-vigrahaḥ = word-division (nom. sg. m.)
• kriyate = is made (3rd sg. pres. pass.) 		[Pupil] said (āha): 'For what (kim) purpose (prayojanam) is word-division (padavigrahaḥ) made (kriyate)?' Pupil questions the methodology - why is grammatical analysis necessary? Pupil: 'For which purpose is a division of words made?'
tad ucyate: arthaprasiddhyartham • tat = that (nom. sg. n.)
• ucyate = is said (3rd sg. pres. pass.)
• artha-prasiddhi-artham = for the sake of establishing meaning (acc. sg. n.) 		The answer to that (tat) is said (ucyate): for the sake of establishing (prasiddhi) [their] significance (artha). Response: to clarify and establish the meaning of each word precisely. The answer to that is: to establish (their) significance.
kasmād arthāprasiddhiḥ padānām • kasmāt = why? from what? (abl. interr.)
• artha-aprasiddhiḥ = non-obviousness of meaning (nom. sg. f.)
• padānām = of words (gen. pl. n.) 		Why (kasmāt) [is there] non-obviousness (aprasiddhiḥ) of meaning (artha) of the words (padānām)? Follow-up question: why isn't the meaning already clear? [Question:] 'Why is the significance of the words not obvious?'
yasmāt pṛthagarthānīha padāni bhavanti • yasmāt = because (conj.)
• pṛthak-arthāni = having distinct meanings (nom. pl. n.)
• iha = here, in this world (adv.)
• padāni = words (nom. pl. n.)
• bhavanti = are, become (3rd pl. pres.) 		Because (yasmāt) words (padāni) here (iha) have (bhavanti) distinct (pṛthak) meanings (arthāni). Answer: because words on earth have multiple, distinct meanings requiring disambiguation. [Answer:] Because words here on earth (iha) have distinct meanings.
yasmād evam hy āha:
yathā vivṛtagātro 'pi śirasi prāvṛto naraḥ |
nābhivyaktim vrajaty evam sūtram vigrahavarjitam ||		 • yasmāt = because
• evam = thus
• hi = indeed
• āha = [someone] said
• yathā = just as
• vivṛta-gātraḥ = with unveiled limbs
• api = even though
• śirasi = on the head (loc.)
• prāvṛtaḥ = veiled, covered
• naraḥ = man
• na = not
• abhivyaktim = manifestation, clarity
• vrajati = goes, attains
• evam = so, thus
• sūtram = sūtra
• vigraha-varjitam = without word-division 		Hence (yasmāt) the following has indeed (hi) been said (āha): "Just as (yathā) a man (naraḥ) whose head (śirasi) is veiled (prāvṛtaḥ) remains obscure, even (api) if his limbs (gātraḥ) are unveiled (vivṛta), so (evam) does a Sūtra (sūtram) without (varjitam) a word division (vigraha)." Scriptural analogy: even with clear parts, if the head (main point) is veiled, nothing is clear. Similarly, without word-analysis, even a sūtra's meaning stays hidden. Hence the following has indeed rightly been said: "Just as a man whose head is veiled remains obscure, even if his limbs are unveiled, so does a Sūtra without a (word) division."
evam arthaprasiddhyartham padavigrahaḥ kriyate • evam = thus
• artha-prasiddhi-artham = for establishing meaning
• pada-vigrahaḥ = word-division
• kriyate = is made 		Thus (evam), word-division (padavigrahaḥ) is made (kriyate) for the sake of establishing (prasiddhi) [their] significance (artha). Conclusion: this is why we do grammatical analysis - to clarify meaning. Hence the division of words is made in order to establish (their) significance.
EXTENT AND STRUCTURE OF THE ŚĀSTRA
āha: uktaḥ padavigrahaḥ prayojanam ca | idam tu vācyam: atha śāstrādiḥ ka iti • āha = [pupil] said
• uktaḥ = told, stated (nom. sg. m. PPP)
• pada-vigrahaḥ = word-division
• prayojanam = purpose
• ca = and
• idam = this
• tu = but
• vācyam = to be said (FPP)
• atha = now, well then
• śāstra-ādiḥ = beginning of the śāstra
• kaḥ = what? (nom. sg. m.)
• iti = thus 		[Pupil] said (āha): 'The word-division and its purpose have been told; but this remains to be told: what, then, is the beginning of the Śāstra?' Transition to next question: what constitutes the opening/beginning of this teaching? Pupil: 'The division of words and its purpose have been told; but this remains to be told: what, then, is the beginning of the Śāstra?'
atrocyate: athātaḥ paśupater ity eṣa tāvac chāstrādiḥ • atra = here
• ucyate = it is said
• atha-ataḥ = atha and ataḥ
• paśu-pateḥ = of Paśupati
• iti = thus
• eṣaḥ = this
• tāvat = indeed, certainly
• śāstra-ādiḥ = beginning of the śāstra 		Here it is said: 'Certainly (atha), therefore (ataḥ), of Paśupati (paśupateḥ)' - these (eṣaḥ) words are indeed (tāvat) the beginning (ādiḥ) of the Śāstra (śāstra). Answer: the opening words of PS 1.1 constitute the śāstra's beginning. Here it is said: 'Certainly, therefore, of Paśupati'. These words are indeed the beginning of the Śāstra.
tatra śāstram tantram grantho vidyā ca • tatra = in this case, therein
• śāstram = teaching, śāstra
• tantram = system
• granthaḥ = text
• vidyā = knowledge, insight
• ca = and 		In this case (tatra), 'śāstra' (śāstram), that is system (tantram), is text (granthaḥ) and (ca) insight into reality (vidyā). Definition: śāstra encompasses both textual form (grantha) and realized knowledge (vidyā). In this case 'Śāstra', that is system (tantra), is text (grantha) and insight into reality (vidyā).
granthārthayos tadadhigamopāyatvāt • grantha-arthayoḥ = of text and meaning (gen. dual)
• tat-adhigama-upāyatvāt = because of being the means of understanding that (abl.) 		Because (tvāt) text and reality (granthārthayoḥ) are the means (upāyatvāt) of understanding (adhigama) that (tat) (Śāstra). Explanation: both written text and its meaning/reality serve as instruments for comprehending the śāstra. Because text and reality are the means of understanding (adhigama) that (Śāstra).
pārimāṇyam athaśabdādiśivāntam pravacanam • pārimāṇyam = as regards extent/measure
• atha-śabda-ādi = beginning with the word "atha"
• śiva-antam = ending with "śiva"
• pravacanam = doctrine, teaching 		As regards extent (pārimāṇyam): the doctrine (pravacanam) begins with (ādi) the word (śabda) 'certainly' (atha) (PS 1.1) and ends with (antam) 'śiva' (śiva) (PS 5.47). Defines the textual boundaries: from first word of first sūtra to last word of last sūtra. As regards (its) extent: the doctrine (pravacana) begins with the word 'certainly' (PS 1.1) and ends with 'śiva' (PS 5.47).
saṃkhyā pañcādhyāyāḥ pañca brahmāṇi • saṃkhyā = as regards number
• pañca-adhyāyāḥ = five chapters
• pañca = five
• brahmāṇi = Brahmans (sections) 		As regards number (saṃkhyā): there are five (pañca) chapters (adhyāyāḥ) and five (pañca) Brahmans (brahmāṇi). Structural organization: the text has five chapters (adhyāya) called five Brahmans. As regards number: there are five chapters and five Brahmans.
adhikaraṇam ca athaśabdāt śabdavyākhyānavacanāt snānaśayanādyupadeśāc ca śiṣyācāryayoḥ prasiddhiḥ • adhikaraṇam = empowerment, authority (nom.)
• ca = and
• atha-śabdāt = from the word "atha"
• śabda-vyākhyāna-vacanāt = from speaking of word-explanation
• snāna-śayana-ādi-upadeśāt = from instruction regarding bathing, lying down, etc.
• ca = and
• śiṣya-ācāryayoḥ = of pupil and teacher (gen. dual)
• prasiddhiḥ = establishment (nom.) 		And (ca) as regards empowerment (adhikaraṇam): the establishment (prasiddhiḥ) of the (relationship between) the preceptor and pupil (śiṣyācāryayoḥ) is warranted by the word (śabdāt) 'certainly' (atha), the word 'therefore' and (ca) 'explaining' (vyākhyānavacanāt), as well as by the instructions (upadeśāt), such as (ādi) those regarding bathing (snāna) and lying down (śayana). Explains adhikāra (qualification/authorization): specific sūtra words and content establish who is qualified to teach and learn. And as regards empowering/confirmation (adhikaraṇa): the establishment of the (relationship between) the preceptor and pupil is warranted by the (Sūtra) word 'certainly', the word 'therefore' and 'explaining', as well as by the instructions (upadeśa), such as those regarding bathing and lying down.
THE TEACHER'S PRE-EMINENCE AMONG ALL TEACHERS
kaivalyagatānām api duḥkhitvadarśanāt • kaivalya-gatānām = of those who have reached isolation/liberation (gen. pl.)
• api = even
• duḥkhitva-darśanāt = from seeing suffering (abl.) 		[The preceptor meant here is the best of all preceptors], because (darśanāt) we see that even (api) those who have reached (gatānām) isolation (kaivalya) are still affected by suffering (duḥkhitva) [and he is not]. First argument for teacher's supremacy: even liberated yogins (kaivalya-gata) still experience duḥkha, but this teacher doesn't. [The preceptor meant here is the best of all preceptors], because we see that even those who have reached isolation (kaivalya) are still affected by suffering [and he is not].
kāryakāraṇapratyakṣadarśī vipratvāt • kārya-kāraṇa-pratyakṣa-darśī = one who has direct vision of body and senses
• vipratvāt = from being omniscient (abl.) 		On the strength of (vipratvāt) 'He is omniscient' (vipratva) (PS 5.26), (we know that) he has a direct (pratyakṣa) (infallible) vision (darśī) of body (kārya) and senses (kāraṇa). Second argument: citing PS 5.26 (vipratva = omniscience), the teacher has pratyakṣa (direct perception) of both body (kārya) and senses (kāraṇa). On the strength of 'He is omniscient' (vipratva) (PS 5.26), (we know that) he has a direct (infallible) vision of creation (kārya) and of Creator (kāraṇa).
upāyopeyapratyakṣadarśitvāc ca praśnaprativaktā • upāya-upeya-pratyakṣa-darśitvāt = from having direct vision of means and end (abl.)
• ca = and
• praśna-prati-vaktā = answerer of questions (nom.) 		He can (truly) answer (prati) questions (praśna), because (darśitvāt) he has (ca) a direct (pratyakṣa) (infallible) vision (darśitvāt) of means (upāya) and end (upeya). Third argument: ability to answer questions authoritatively stems from direct perception of upāya (means/path) and upeya (goal/end). He can (truly) answer questions, because he has a direct (infallible) vision of means and end.
aiśvaryāvasthā caiva muktatvān • aiśvarya-avasthā = state of absolute sovereignty
• ca = and
• eva = indeed
• muktatvāt = from being liberated (abl.) 		[Of] absolute sovereignty (aiśvarya) [the] state (avasthā) and (ca) indeed (eva) from being liberated (muktatvāt). Fourth argument: liberation (muktatva) results in aiśvarya-avasthā (state of supreme lordship/sovereignty). He is in a state of absolute sovereignty (aiśvarya) because he is liberated.
manonmanaḥsaṃsthaś ca kāmitvāt • manas-unmanaḥ-saṃsthaḥ = one established in rational and exalted mental states
• ca = and
• kāmitvāt = from wish-fulfillment power (abl.) 		And (ca) he assumes (saṃsthaḥ) rational and exalted states (saṃsthaḥ) of mind (manonmanaḥ), as follows from (kāmitvāt) 'He can do whatever he wishes' (kāmitva) (PS 1.24). Fifth argument: citing PS 1.24, the teacher possesses kāmitva (power of wish-fulfillment), demonstrating control over manas-unmanah (ordinary and elevated consciousness states). And he assumes rational and exalted states of mind (manonmanaḥ), as follows from 'He can do whatever he wishes' (kāmitva) (PS 1.24).
ataḥ sarvācāryaviśiṣṭo 'yam ācāryaḥ • ataḥ = therefore
• sarva-ācārya-viśiṣṭaḥ = pre-eminent above all teachers
• ayam = this
• ācāryaḥ = teacher (nom.) 		Therefore (ataḥ) this (ayam) preceptor (ācāryaḥ) is pre-eminent (viśiṣṭaḥ) above all (sarva) preceptors (ācārya). Conclusion: based on five arguments (freedom from suffering, omniscience, knowledge of means/end, sovereignty, wish-fulfillment), this teacher surpasses all others. Therefore this preceptor is pre-eminent above all preceptors.
THE STUDENT'S QUALIFICATIONS
iti | tathā brahmaṇagrahaṇāt stripratiṣedhād indriyajayopadeśāc ca • iti = therefore
• tathā = likewise
• brahmaṇa-grahaṇāt = from the specification of a Brahmin (abl. sg.)
• strī-pratiṣedhāt = from the prohibition regarding women (abl. sg.)
• indriya-jaya-upadeśāt = from the teaching about sense-control (abl. sg.)
• ca = and 		Therefore (iti), likewise (tathā) [as with the teacher's excellence], from (grahaṇāt) the scriptural specification [requiring the student to be] a Brahmin (brahmaṇa), from (pratiṣedhāt) the prohibition regarding women (strī) [as students], and (ca) from (upadeśāt) the teaching about sense (indriya)-conquest (jaya). Creates a parallel to the teacher's pre-eminence: "tathā" (likewise/just so) indicates that just as the teacher has been shown to be supreme, so too the student is distinguished above all other students based on scriptural qualifications - Brahmin birth (PS 4.20), male gender (prohibition of women, PS 1.13), and mastery of senses (PS 5.7). Just so, on the strength of the Sūtras mentioning brāhmaṇa, forbidding [intercourse] with women and instructing the conquest of the senses...
uktaṃ hi: • uktam = it has been said (nom. sg., past pass. part.)
• hi = for, indeed 		For (hi) it has been said (uktam). Introduces scriptural citation as authoritative support. As it has been said [in scripture]:
bādhiryam āndhyam aghratvam mukatā jaḍatā tathā |

• tathā = likewise
