De-sandhi:
antaḥ-niścalita-ātma-dīpa-kalikā-sva-ādhāra-bandha-ādibhiḥ
yaḥ yogī yuga-kalpa-kāla-kalanāt tattvam ca jegīyate |
jñāna-āmoda-mahā-udadhiḥ samabhavat yatra Ādināṭhaḥ svayam
vyakta-avyakta-guṇa-adhikam tam aniśam śrī-Mīnanātham bhaje ||		 antaḥ-niścalita-ātma-dīpa-kalikā = in flame of soul-lamp steadied within
sva-ādhāra-bandha-ādibhiḥ = by locking own base etc. (inst.)
yaḥ yogī = which yogi (nom.)
yuga-kalpa-kāla-kalanāt = through understanding yugas, kalpas, time
tattvam = reality (acc.)
jegīyate = is thoroughly proclaimed
jñāna-āmoda-mahā-udadhiḥ = great ocean of knowledge-bliss (nom.)
samabhavat = became/occurred (3rd sg. past)
yatra = where (rel. adv.)
Ādināṭhaḥ = Ādinātha (nom.)
svayam = himself
vyakta-avyakta-guṇa-adhikam = greater than manifest-unmanifest qualities (acc.)
tam = him (acc.)
aniśam = constantly
Mīnanātham = Matsyendranātha (acc.)
bhaje = I worship (1st sg.)		 The yogi (yaḥ yogī) by locking own base etc. (svādhārabandhādibhiḥ) in the flame of the soul-lamp steadied within (antarniścalitātmadīpakalikā), through understanding (kalanāt) of yugas, kalpas, and time (yugakalpakāla), by whom reality (tattvam) is thoroughly proclaimed (jegīyate), who became (samabhavat) [that state] where (yatra) Ādinātha himself (Ādināṭhaḥ svayam) [appeared as] a great ocean of knowledge-bliss (jñānāmodamahodadhiḥ), [who is] greater than manifest and unmanifest qualities (vyaktāvyaktaguṇādhikam)—him (tam), the glorious Matsyendranātha (śrīmīnanātham), I constantly (aniśam) worship (bhaje). Praise of Matsyendranātha as embodiment of Ādinātha
[√bhaj - to worship, √jñā - to know, √bhū - to become]		 The yogi who, by means of locking the base and so forth in the buds (flames, kalikās) of the internally stilled lamp of the self, is extolled as (extols?) the essence of creating the yugas, kalpas and time (?), in whom Ādinātha himself appeared, the great ocean of knowledge and pleasure; him do I constantly worship as the glorious Mīnanātha, who abounds in the manifest and unmanifest qualities (?).
namaskṛtya guruṃ bhaktyā gorakṣo jñānamuttamam |
abhīṣṭaṃ yogināṃ brūte paramānandakārakam ||3||

De-sandhi:
namaskṛtya gurum bhaktyā Gorakṣaḥ jñānam uttamam |
abhīṣṭam yoginām brūte parama-ānanda-kārakam ||		 namaskṛtya = having saluted (abs.)
gurum = guru (acc.)
bhaktyā = with devotion (inst.)
Gorakṣaḥ = Gorakṣa (nom.)
jñānam uttamam = supreme knowledge (acc.)
abhīṣṭam = desired (acc.)
yoginām = of yogis (gen.)
brūte = speaks (3rd sg.)
parama-ānanda-kārakam = causing supreme bliss (acc.)		 Having saluted (namaskṛtya) the guru (gurum) with devotion (bhaktyā), Gorakṣa (Gorakṣaḥ) speaks (brūte) supreme knowledge (jñānam uttamam), desired (abhīṣṭam) of yogis (yoginām), causing supreme bliss (paramānandakārakam). Gorakṣa's teaching of supreme knowledge
[√kṛ - to do, √brū - to speak]		 Having devotedly made obeisance to [him, his] guru, Gorakṣa teaches the highest knowledge, which is longed for by yogis and brings about supreme bliss.
gorakṣaśatakaṃ vakti yogināṃ hitakāmyayā |
dhruvaṃ yasyāvabodhena jāyate paramaṃ padam ||4||

De-sandhi:
gorakṣa-śatakam vakti yoginām hita-kāmyayā |
dhruvam yasya avabodhena jāyate paramam padam ||		 gorakṣa-śatakam = hundred verses of Gorakṣa (acc.)
vakti = speaks (3rd sg.)
yoginām = of yogis (gen.)
hita-kāmyayā = with desire for welfare (inst.)
dhruvam = certainly (ind.)
yasya = of which (gen.)
avabodhena = by understanding (inst.)
jāyate = arises (3rd sg.)
paramam padam = supreme state (nom.)		 He speaks (vakti) the hundred verses of Gorakṣa (gorakṣaśatakam) with desire for the welfare (hitakāmyayā) of yogis (yoginām), by understanding (avabodhena) of which (yasya) certainly (dhruvam) arises (jāyate) the supreme state (paramaṃ padam). Purpose of the Gorakṣaśataka
[√vac - to speak, √jan - to arise]		 Out of a desire for the good of yogis, he teaches the hundred [verses] of Gorakṣa, understanding of which is sure to bring about the supreme state.
etat vimukti-sopānam etat kālasya vañcanam |
yad vyāvṛttaṃ mano bhogād āsaktaṃ paramātmani ||1||

De-sandhi:
etat vimukti-sopānam etat kālasya vañcanam |
yad vyā-āvṛttam manaḥ bhogāt āsaktam parama-ātmani ||		 vimukti-sopānam = ladder to liberation (TP, nom.)
kālasya = of time/death (gen.)
vañcanam = deceiving (nom.)
yad = when/because (rel.)
vyā-āvṛttam = turned away (PPP, nom.)
manaḥ = mind (nom.)
bhogāt = from enjoyment (abl.)
āsaktam = attached (PPP, nom.)
parama-ātmani = in supreme Self (loc.)		 This (etat) is the ladder to liberation (vimuktisopānam), this is deceiving death (kālasya vañcanam)—when (yad) the mind (manaḥ) is turned away (vyāvṛttam) from worldly enjoyment (bhogāt) and attached (āsaktam) to the supreme Self (paramātmani). Mind turned from enjoyment to Supreme Self
[√vṛt - to turn, √sañj - to attach, √vañc - to deceive]		 This is the stairway to complete liberation, this is the cheating of death, by which the mind is turned away from worldly enjoyment and fixed in the supreme self.
dvija-sevita-śākhasya śruti-kalpa-taroḥ phalam |
śamanaṃ bhava-tāpasya yogaṃ bhajeta sattamāḥ ||2||

De-sandhi:
dvija-sevita-śākhasya śruti-kalpa-taroḥ phalam |
śamanam bhava-tāpasya yogam bhajeta sat-tamāḥ ||		 dvija-sevita-śākhasya = whose branches served by twice-born (BV, gen.)
śruti-kalpa-taroḥ = of wish-fulfilling tree of Vedas (gen.)
phalam = fruit (nom.)

bhava-tāpasya = of pain of worldly existence (gen.)
yogam = yoga (acc.)
bhajeta = should resort to (opt.)

O best of people (sattamāḥ), partake of (bhajeta) yoga (yogam), the fruit (phalam) of the wish-fulfilling tree of Vedic revelation (śrutikalpa-taroḥ) whose branches are frequented by the twice-born (dvijasevitaśākhasya), which soothes (śamanam) the torment of existence (bhavatāpasya). Yoga as fruit of Vedic wisdom
[√bhaj - to partake, √śam - to soothe]		 O excellent people, partake of yoga, the reward of the wish-fulfilling tree of revelation frequented by the twice-born, which soothes the torment of existence.
āsanaṃ prāṇa-saṃrodhaḥ pratyāhāraś ca dhāraṇā |
dhyānaṃ samādhir etāni yogāṅgāni bhavanti ṣaṭ ||3||

De-sandhi:
āsanam prāṇa-saṃrodhaḥ pratyāhāraḥ ca dhāraṇā |

prāṇa-saṃrodhaḥ = breath restraint (TP, nom.)

ṣaṭ = six		 Posture (āsanam), breath restraint (prāṇasaṃrodhaḥ), withdrawal (pratyāhāraḥ), concentration (dhāraṇā), meditation (dhyānam), and absorption (samādhiḥ)—these (etāni) are the six (ṣaṭ) limbs of Yoga (yogāṅgāni). Six limbs of yoga enumerated
[√bhū - to be, √rudh - to restrain]		 Posture, breath restraint (prāṇasaṃrodha), withdrawal, fixation, meditation and samādhi: these are the six auxiliaries of yoga.
āsanāni ca tāvanti yāvantyo jīva-jātayaḥ |
eteṣām akhilān bhedān vijānāti maheśvaraḥ ||4||

De-sandhi:
āsanāni ca tāvanti yāvantyaḥ jīva-jātayaḥ |
eteṣām akhilān bhedān vijānāti maheśvaraḥ ||		 āsanāni = postures (nom. pl.)
tāvanti = so many (nom. pl.)
yāvantyaḥ = as many as (nom. pl. f.)
jīva-jātayaḥ = species of living beings (TP, nom. pl.)

akhilān = all (acc. pl.)
bhedān = variations (acc. pl.)
vijānāti = knows (3rd sg.)
maheśvaraḥ = the great Lord, Shiva (nom.)		 There are as many (tāvanti) postures (āsanāni) as there are (yāvantyaḥ) species of living beings (jīvajātayaḥ). Maheśvara (maheśvaraḥ) knows (vijānāti) all (akhilān) their variations (bhedān). As many postures as living beings
[√jñā - to know]		 There are as many postures as there are types of living being. Maheśvara knows all their varieties.
catur-āśīti-lakṣāṇām ekaikaṃ samudāhṛtam |
ataḥ śivena pīṭhānāṃ ṣoḍaśonaṃ śataṃ kṛtam ||5||

De-sandhi:
catuḥ-aśīti-lakṣāṇām ekaikam sam-ud-āhṛtam |
ataḥ śivena pīṭhānām ṣoḍaśa-ūnam śatam kṛtam ||		 catuḥ-aśīti-lakṣāṇām = of 84 hundred-thousands (gen. pl.)
ekaikam = one each (nom.)

pīṭhānām = of postures (gen. pl.)
ṣoḍaśa-ūnam = diminished by sixteen
śatam = hundred (nom.)
kṛtam = was made (PPP, nom.)		 From the 8,400,000 (caturaśītilakṣāṇām), one each (ekaikam) was selected (samudāhṛtam); therefore (ataḥ) Śiva (śivena) made (kṛtam) a hundred diminished by sixteen (ṣoḍaśonaṃ śatam) postures (pīṭhānām). 84 primary postures selected
[√kṛ - to make, √ūn - to lack/lessen]		 Śiva taught the 84 lakh positions one by one, then made them 84.
āsanebhyaḥ samastebhyo dvayam etad udāhṛtam |
ekaṃ siddhāsanaṃ proktaṃ dvitīyaṃ kamalāsanam ||6||

De-sandhi:
āsanebhyaḥ samastebhyaḥ dvayam etad ud-āhṛtam |
ekam siddha-āsanam proktam dvitīyam kamala-āsanam ||		 āsanebhyaḥ = from the postures (abl. pl.)
samastebhyaḥ = from all (abl. pl.)
dvayam = pair (nom.)
etad = this (nom.)
ud-āhṛtam = is selected/mentioned (PPP, nom.)
ekam = first (nom.)
siddha-āsanam = perfect posture (TP, nom.)
proktam = is called (PPP, nom.)
dvitīyam = second (nom.)
kamala-āsanam = lotus posture (TP, nom.)		 From all (samastebhyaḥ) the postures (āsanebhyaḥ), this pair (dvayam etad) is selected (udāhṛtam): the first (ekam) is called (proktam) the perfect posture (siddhāsanam), the second (dvitīyam) the lotus posture (kamalāsanam). Two chief postures: Siddha and Padma
[√sidh - to accomplish, √pad - to go/be]		 From all the postures this pair is taught: one called siddhāsana, "the adept's posture", the other kamalāsana, "the lotus posture".
yoni-sthānakam āṅghri-mūla-ghaṭitaṃ kṛtvā dṛḍhaṃ vinyasen
meḍhre pādam athaikam eva hṛdaye dhṛtvā hanuṃ su-sthiram |
sthāṇuḥ saṃyamitendriyoacala-dṛśā paśyed bhruvor antaraṃ
hy etan mokṣa-kapāṭa-bheda-janakaṃ siddhāsanaṃ procyate ||7||

De-sandhi:
yoni-sthānakam āṅghri-mūla-ghaṭitam kṛtvā dṛḍham vinyaset
meḍhre pādam atha ekam eva hṛdaye dhṛtvā hanum su-sthiram |
sthāṇuḥ saṃyamita-indriyaḥ acala-dṛśā paśyet bhruvoḥ antaram
hi etat mokṣa-kapāṭa-bheda-janakam siddha-āsanam procyate ||		 yoni-sthānakam = perineum (acc.)
āṅghri-mūla-ghaṭitam = connected with heel (acc.)
kṛtvā = having made (abs.)
dṛḍham = firmly (adv.)
vinyaset = should place (opt.)
meḍhre = on genitals (loc.)
pādam = foot (acc.)
atha = then
ekam eva = one only
hṛdaye = at heart (loc.)
dhṛtvā = having held (abs.)
hanum = chin (acc.)
su-sthiram = very firmly
sthāṇuḥ = motionless (nom.)
saṃyamita-indriyaḥ = with controlled senses (BV, nom.)
acala-dṛśā = with steady gaze (inst.)
paśyet = should look (opt.)
bhruvoḥ = of eyebrows (gen. dual)
antaram = between (acc.)
mokṣa-kapāṭa-bheda-janakam = causing breaking of door to liberation (BV, nom.)
siddha-āsanam = perfect posture (nom.)
procyate = is called (pass.)		 Having firmly (dṛḍham kṛtvā) placed the root of the heel (āṅghrimūlaghaṭitam) at the perineum (yonisthānakam), one should place (vinyaset) the other foot (pādam ekam eva) on the genitals (meḍhre). Having held (dhṛtvā) the chin (hanum) very firmly (su-sthiram) at the heart (hṛdaye), motionless (sthāṇuḥ), with controlled senses (saṃyamitendriyaḥ) and steady gaze (acaladṛśā), one should look (paśyet) between the eyebrows (bhruvoḥ antaram). This (etat) is called (procyate) the perfect posture (siddhāsanam), which breaks open the door to liberation (mokṣakapāṭabhedajanakam). Siddhasana description and benefits
[√kṛ - to make, √dhṛ - to hold, √paś - to see, √bhid - to break]		 [The yogi] should place the root of the heel at the perineum and firmly place the other foot on the penis. He should hold his jaw very steadily on his chest and, motionless, with his sense-organs restrained, stare with fixed gaze at the space between the eyebrows. This is called the adept's posture. It opens the doorway to liberation.
vāmorūpari dakṣiṇaṃ ca caraṇaṃ saṃsthāpya vāmaṃ tathā
yāmyorūpari paścimena vidhinā dhṛtvā karābhyāṃ dṛḍham |
aṅguṣṭhe hṛdaye nidhāya cibukam nāsāgramālokayet
etad dhādhivikārahāri yamināṃ padmāsanaṃ procyate ||8||

De-sandhi:
vāma-ūru-upari dakṣiṇam ca caraṇam saṃsthāpya vāmam tathā
yāmya-ūru-upari paścimena vidhinā dhṛtvā karābhyām dṛḍham |
aṅguṣṭhe hṛdaye nidhāya cibukam nāsā-agram ālokayet
etat vyādhi-vikāra-hāri yaminām padma-āsanam procyate ||		 vāma-ūru-upari = upon left thigh
dakṣiṇam = right (acc.)
caraṇam = foot (acc.)
saṃsthāpya = having placed (abs.)
vāmam = left (acc.)
tathā = likewise
yāmya-ūru-upari = upon right thigh
paścimena vidhinā = by back method (inst.)
dhṛtvā = having held (abs.)
karābhyām = with both hands (inst. du.)
dṛḍham = firmly (adv.)
aṅguṣṭhe = big toes (loc.)
hṛdaye = at heart (loc.)
nidhāya = placing (abs.)
cibukam = chin (acc.)
nāsā-agram = tip of nose (acc.)
ālokayet = should gaze (opt.)
vyādhi-vikāra-hāri = remover of disease-disorder (BV)
yaminām = of self-restrained (gen. pl.)
padma-āsanam = lotus-posture (nom.)
procyate = is called (pass.)		 Having placed (saṃsthāpya) the right foot (dakṣiṇaṃ caraṇam) on the left thigh (vāmorūpari), and likewise (tathā) the left (vāmam) on the right thigh (yāmyorūpari), and having firmly held (dhṛtvā dṛḍham) the big toes (aṅguṣṭhe) with both hands (karābhyām) by the back method (paścimena vidhinā), placing (nidhāya) the chin (cibukam) at the heart (hṛdaye), one should gaze (ālokayet) at the tip of the nose (nāsāgram). This (etat) is called (procyate) the lotus posture (padmāsanam) of the self-restrained (yaminām), which removes disease and disorder (vyādhivikārahāri). Padmasana description and benefits
[√sthā - to place, √dhṛ - to hold, √lok - to gaze, √hṛ - to remove]		 [The yogi] should place his right foot on his left thigh and his left foot on his right thigh, with his hands going behind his back hold firmly on to his big toes, place his chin on his chest and look at the tip of his nose. This is called the lotus posture. It removes sicknesses and diseases from those who restrain themselves.
ṣaṭcakraṃ ṣoḍaśādhāraṃ trailokyaṃ vyomapañcakam |
svadehe ye na jānanti kathaṃ sidhyanti yoginaḥ ||9||

De-sandhi:
ṣaṭ-cakram ṣoḍaśa-ādhāram trai-lokyam vyoma-pañcakam |
sva-dehe ye na jānanti katham sidhyanti yoginaḥ ||		 ṣaṭ-cakram = six chakras (acc.)
ṣoḍaśa-ādhāram = sixteen supports (acc.)
trai-lokyam = three worlds (acc.)
vyoma-pañcakam = five voids (acc.)
sva-dehe = in own body (loc.)
ye = who (nom. pl.)
jānanti = know (3rd pl.)
katham = how
sidhyanti = attain perfection (3rd pl.)
yoginaḥ = yogis (nom. pl.)		 Those who (ye) do not know (na jānanti) in their own bodies (svadehe) the six chakras (ṣaṭcakram), sixteen supports (ṣoḍaśādhāram), three worlds (trailokyam), and five voids (vyomapañcakam)—how (katham) can yogis (yoginaḥ) attain perfection (sidhyanti)? Knowledge of six chakras essential for perfection
[√jñā - to know, √sidh - to perfect]		 Those who do not recognise the six cakras, sixteen supports, three worlds [and] five voids in their own bodies, how can they become perfected yogis?
ekastambhaṃ navadvāraṃ triśūnyaṃ pañcadaivatam |
svadehe ye na jānanti kathaṃ sidhyanti yoginaḥ ||10||

De-sandhi:
eka-stambham nava-dvāram tri-śūnyam pañca-daivatam |
sva-dehe ye na jānanti katham sidhyanti yoginaḥ ||		 eka-stambham = one pillar (acc.)
nava-dvāram = nine gates (acc.)
tri-śūnyam = three voids (acc.)
pañca-daivatam = five deities (acc.)
sva-dehe = in own body (loc.)
ye = who (nom. pl.)
jānanti = know (3rd pl.)
katham = how
sidhyanti = attain perfection (3rd pl.)
yoginaḥ = yogis (nom. pl.)		 Those who (ye) do not know (na jānanti) in their own bodies (svadehe) the single pillar (ekastambham), nine gates (navadvāram), three voids (triśūnyam), and five deities (pañcadaivatam)—how (katham) can yogis (yoginaḥ) attain perfection (sidhyanti)? Knowledge of body's pillars and gates essential
[√jñā - to know, √sidh - to perfect]		 Those who do not recognise the single column, the nine doors, the three voids [and] the five deities in their own bodies, how can they become perfected yogis?
caturdalaṃ syād ādhāraṃ svādhiṣṭhānaṃ ca ṣaḍdalam |
nābhau daśadalaṃ padmaṃ sūryasaṅkhyādalaṃ hṛdi ||11||

De-sandhi:
catuḥ-dalam syāt ādhāram svādhiṣṭhānam ca ṣaṭ-dalam |
nābhau daśa-dalam padmam sūrya-saṅkhyā-dalam hṛdi ||		 catuḥ-dalam = four-petaled (nom.)
syāt = is (opt.)
ādhāram = ādhāra/mūlādhāra (nom.)
svādhiṣṭhānam = svādhiṣṭhāna (nom.)
ṣaṭ-dalam = six-petaled (nom.)
nābhau = at navel (loc.)
daśa-dalam = ten-petaled (nom.)
padmam = lotus (nom.)
sūrya-saṅkhyā-dalam = sun-number-petaled (nom.)
hṛdi = at heart (loc.)		 The Base (ādhāram) is (syāt) four-petaled (caturdalam), the Svādhiṣṭhāna (svādhiṣṭhānam) is six-petaled (ṣaḍdalam). At the navel (nābhau) is a ten-petaled (daśadalam) lotus (padmam), and at the heart (hṛdi) one with the number of the sun's petals (sūryasaṅkhyādalam, i.e., twelve). Four lower chakras with petal counts
[√as - to be (syāt)]		 The Base (ādhāra) had four petals and the Svādhiṣṭhāna has six petals. In the navel there is a lotus with ten petals [and the lotus] in the heart has twelve petals.
kaṇṭhe syāt ṣoḍaśadalaṃ bhrumadhye dvidalaṃ tathā |
sahasradalam ākhyātam brahmarandhre mahāpathe ||12||

De-sandhi:
kaṇṭhe syāt ṣoḍaśa-dalam bhru-madhye dvi-dalam tathā |
sahasra-dalam ākhyātam brahma-randhre mahā-pathe ||		 kaṇṭhe = in throat (loc.)
syāt = is (opt.)
ṣoḍaśa-dalam = sixteen-petaled (nom.)
bhru-madhye = between eyebrows (loc.)
dvi-dalam = two-petaled (nom.)
tathā = likewise
sahasra-dalam = thousand-petaled (nom.)
ākhyātam = called (PPP, nom.)
brahma-randhre = at brahmarandhra (loc.)
mahā-pathe = on great path (loc.)		 In the throat (kaṇṭhe) is (syāt) a sixteen-petaled (ṣoḍaśadalam) [lotus], and likewise (tathā) between the eyebrows (bhrumadhye) a two-petaled one (dvidalam). The thousand-petaled (sahasradalam) [lotus] is said (ākhyātam) to be at the brahmarandhra (brahmarandhre), on the great path (mahāpathe). Three upper chakras with petal counts
[√as - to be (syāt), √khyā - to call]		 In the throat is [a lotus] with sixteen petals and between the eyebrows [a lotus] with two petals. [The lotus] that is taught to have a thousand petals is in the great pathway at the aperture of Brahman.
ādhāraṃ prathamaṃ cakraṃ svādhiṣṭhānaṃ dvitīyakam |
yonisthānaṃ tayoḥ madhye kāmarūpam pracakṣate ||13||

De-sandhi:
ādhāram prathamam cakram svādhiṣṭhānam dvitīyakam |
yoni-sthānam tayoḥ madhye kāma-rūpam pracakṣate ||		 ādhāram = ādhāra/mūlādhāra (nom.)
prathamam = first (nom.)
cakram = cakra (nom.)
svādhiṣṭhānam = svādhiṣṭhāna (nom.)
dvitīyakam = second (nom.)
yoni-sthānam = yonisthāna/perineal region (acc.)
tayoḥ = of those two (gen. dual)
madhye = in middle (loc.)
kāma-rūpam = kāmarūpa (acc.)
pracakṣate = they call (3rd pl. mid.)		 The Base (ādhāram) is the first (prathamam) chakra (cakram), Svādhiṣṭhāna (svādhiṣṭhānam) is the second (dvitīyakam). The perineal region (yonisthānam) in the middle (madhye) of those two (tayoḥ) is called (pracakṣate) Kāmarūpa (kāmarūpam). Location of Kāmarūpa between two chakras
[√cakṣ - to call/see]		 The Base (ādhāram) is the first cakra, Svādhiṣṭhāna is second. The perineal region (yonisthānam) between them is called Kāmarūpa.
adhomukhaṃ gudasthāne paṅkajam yaccaturdalam |
tanmadhye procyate yoniḥ kāmākhyā siddhavanditā ||14||

De-sandhi:
adhaḥ-mukham guda-sthāne paṅkajam yat catuḥ-dalam |
tat-madhye procyate yoniḥ kāmākhyā siddha-vanditā ||		 adhaḥ-mukham = downward-facing (nom.)
guda-sthāne = at place of anus (loc.)
paṅkajam = lotus (nom.)
yat = which (rel. pron.)
catuḥ-dalam = four-petaled (nom.)
tat-madhye = in middle of that (loc.)
procyate = is proclaimed (pass.)
yoniḥ = yoni/source (nom.)
kāmākhyā = called Kāmākhyā (nom.)
siddha-vanditā = by-Siddhas-worshipped (nom.)		 The downward-facing (adhomukham) four-petaled (yaccaturdalam) lotus (paṅkajam) at the location of the anus (gudasthāne)—in its middle (tanmadhye) is proclaimed (procyate) the yoni (yoniḥ), called Kāmākhyā (kāmākhyā), worshipped by the Siddhas (siddhavanditā). Mūlādhāra lotus with yoni Kāmākhyā
[√vand - to worship]		 The lotus with four petals at the location of the anus faces downwards. The yoni in its middle is called Kāmā and is worshipped by adepts.
yonimadhye mahāliṅgam paścimābhimukhaṃ sthitam |
mastake maṇivad bhinnam yo jānāti sa yogavit ||15||

De-sandhi:
yoni-madhye mahā-liṅgam paścima-abhimukham sthitam |
mastake maṇi-vat bhinnam yaḥ jānāti sa yoga-vit ||		 yoni-madhye = in middle of yoni (loc.)
mahā-liṅgam = great liṅga (nom.)
paścima-abhimukham = facing westward (nom.)
sthitam = situated (PPP, nom.)
mastake = at top (loc.)
maṇi-vat = like jewel (adv.)
bhinnam = split (PPP, nom.)
yaḥ = who (rel. pron.)
jānāti = knows (3rd sg.)
yoga-vit = knower of yoga (nom.)		 In the middle of the yoni (yonimadhye) is situated (sthitam) the great liṅga (mahāliṅgam) facing rearward (paścimābhimukham), split (bhinnam) at the top (mastake) like a jewel (maṇivat). He who (yo) knows (jānāti) this is (sa) a knower of yoga (yogavit). Great liṅga in yoni facing rearward
[√jñā - to know, √sthā - to stand, √bhid - to split]		 In the middle of the yoni is situated a great liṅga facing rearwards. He who knows the blown [lotus] in the head that is like a jewel knows yoga.
taptacāmīkarābhāsam taḍillekheva visphurat |
caturasram puram vahner adho meḍhāt pratiṣṭitam ||16||

De-sandhi:
tapta-cāmīkara-ābhāsam taḍit-lekhā iva visphurat |

vahneḥ = of Fire (gen.)
adhaḥ = below

Below (adhaḥ) the penis (meḍhāt) is situated (pratiṣṭhitam) the four-cornered (caturasram) city (puram) of Fire (vahneḥ), shining (ābhāsam) like heated gold (taptacāmīkara), flashing (visphurat) like a streak of lightning (taḍillekheva). Fire element chakra below genitals
[√sphur - to flash/sparkle, √pra-sthā - to be established]		 Below the penis is situated the four-sided abode of fire, looking like burnished gold, glittering like a streak of lightning.
yat samādhau paraṃ jyotir anantam viśvatomukham |
tasmin dṛṣṭe mahāyoge yātāyātam na vidyate ||17||

De-sandhi:
yat samādhau param jyotiḥ anantam viśvataḥ-mukham |
tasmin dṛṣṭe mahā-yoge yāta-āyātam na vidyate ||		 yat = which (rel. pron.)
samādhau = in samādhi (loc.)

That (yat) supreme (param) light (jyotir) in samādhi (samādhau), infinite (anantam) and facing all directions (viśvatomukham)—when that (tasmin) is seen (dṛṣṭe) in the great yoga (mahāyoge), there is (vidyate) no (na) more coming and going (yātāyātam). Supreme light ends rebirth cycle
[√dṛś - to see, √yā - to go, √ā-yā - to come, √vid - to find]		 When in absorption the supreme boundless light [shining] in all directions is seen [and] the great yoga has arisen, then there is no [more] coming and going [for the yogi].
svaśabdena bhavet prāṇaḥ adhiṣṭhānam ca tadāśrayaḥ |
svādhiṣṭhānam ataḥ cakram meḍhram eva nigadyate ||18||

De-sandhi:
sva-śabdena bhavet prāṇaḥ adhiṣṭhānam ca tat-āśrayaḥ |
sva-adhiṣṭhānam ataḥ cakram meḍhram eva nigadyate ||		 sva-śabdena = by syllable 'sva' (inst.)
bhavet = becomes (opt.)

meḍhram = genital region (acc.)
eva = exactly

Therefore (ataḥ) the chakra (cakram) at the genital region (meḍhram eva) is called (nigadyate) Svādhiṣṭhāna (svādhiṣṭhānam). Svādhiṣṭhāna chakra etymology
[√bhū - to become, √ā-śri - to support/rest upon]		 Prāṇa arises with the word sva and the adhiṣṭhāna (base??) is its support. Because of this the penis is called the Svādhiṣṭhāna cakra.
maṇivat tantunā yatra vāyunā pūryate vapuḥ |

[√pṝ - to fill, √vac - to call/speak]		 The navel region (nābhimaṇḍalam), where the body is filled with breath like a jewel by a thread, that navel region is called the Maṇipūraka cakra.
dvādaśāre mahācakre puṇyapāpaniyantritaḥ |

De-sandhi:

vindati = finds/realizes (pres.)		 In the twelve-spoked (dvādaśāre) great chakra (mahācakre), controlled by merit and sin (puṇyapāpaniyantritaḥ), the soul (jīvaḥ) wanders (bhramati) for as long (tāvat eva) as (yāvat) it does not find (na vindati) reality (tattvam). Twelve-spoked chakra and karma
[√bhram - to wander, √vid - to know/find]		 Bound by its good and bad deeds, the vital principle (jīvaḥ) wanders in the great cakra (anāhata?) with twelve spokes until it finds the ultimate reality (tattvam).
ūrdhvam meḍhrād adho nābheḥ kando yoniḥ khagāṇḍavat |

[√ut-pad - to arise, √sthā - to be situated]		 Above the penis and below the navel is a bulb, a yoni like a bird's egg. In it arise the 72,000 channels.
teṣu nāḍīsahasreṣu dvisaptatiḥ udāhṛtāḥ |

[√vah - to carry, √smṛ - to remember]		 Among those thousands of channels, 72 important ones are said to carry prāṇa; additionally, of those ten are taught.

[√ā-śri - to take shelter/rest, √sthā - to stand]		 Kuhū is in the region of the penis and Śaṅkhini is at the bottom. The ten channels are thus [each] situated at an orifice.
satatam prāṇavāhinyaḥ tisro nāḍyaḥ prakīrtitāḥ |

Three main nāḍīs with lunar/solar/fire deities

vyāno vyāpī śarīreṣu pradhānāḥ pañca vāyavaḥ |
prāṇādhyāḥ pañca vikhyātā nāgādhyāḥ pañca vāyavaḥ ||32||

De-sandhi:
vyānaḥ vyāpī śarīreṣu pradhānāḥ pañca vāyavaḥ |
prāṇa-ādhyāḥ pañca vikhyātāḥ nāga-ādhyāḥ pañca vāyavaḥ ||		 vyānaḥ = Vyāna (nom.)
vyāpī = pervading (nom.)
śarīreṣu = bodies (loc. pl.)
pradhānāḥ = principal (nom. pl.)
pañca = five
vāyavaḥ = vital airs (nom. pl.)
prāṇa-ādhyāḥ = beginning with Prāṇa (nom. pl.)
pañca = five
vikhyātāḥ = well-known (PPP, nom. pl.)
nāga-ādhyāḥ = beginning with Nāga (nom. pl.)
pañca = five
vāyavaḥ = vital airs (nom. pl.)		 Vyāna (vyānaḥ) is all-pervading (vyāpī) in the body (śarīreṣu)—these are the five principal (pañca pradhānāḥ) vital airs (vāyavaḥ). Five (pañca) well-known (vikhyātāḥ) beginning with Prāṇa (prāṇādhyāḥ), and five (pañca) vital airs (vāyavaḥ) beginning with Nāga (nāgādhyāḥ). Vyāna pervades; 5+5 classification of vāyus
[√vi-āp - to pervade, √khyā - to be known]		 Vyāna pervades bodies. The five chief winds [are]: Five breaths beginning with Prāṇa are taught [and] five beginning with Nāga.
udgāre nāga ākhyātaḥ kūrma unmīlane smṛtaḥ |
kṛkaraḥ kṣutkṛj jñeyo devadatto vijṛmbhaṇe ||33||

De-sandhi:
udgāre nāgaḥ ākhyātaḥ kūrmaḥ unmīlane smṛtaḥ |
kṛkaraḥ kṣut-kṛt jñeyaḥ devadattaḥ vijṛmbhaṇe ||		 udgāre = in belching (loc.)
nāgaḥ = Nāga (nom.)
ākhyātaḥ = is called (PPP, nom.)
kūrmaḥ = Kūrma (nom.)
unmīlane = in opening eyes (loc.)
smṛtaḥ = is remembered (PPP, nom.)
kṛkaraḥ = Kṛkara (nom.)
kṣut-kṛt = causing hunger
jñeyaḥ = should be known
devadattaḥ = Devadatta (nom.)
vijṛmbhaṇe = in yawning (loc.)		 Nāga (nāgaḥ) is called (ākhyātaḥ) the one in belching (udgāre), Kūrma (kūrmaḥ) is remembered (smṛtaḥ) in opening the eyes (unmīlane). Kṛkara (kṛkaraḥ) should be known (jñeyaḥ) as causing hunger (kṣutkṛt), and Devadatta (devadattaḥ) in yawning (vijṛmbhaṇe). Functions of subsidiary vāyus
[√khyā - to call/declare, √smṛ - to remember, √jñā - to know]		 Nāga is taught [to be active] when belching, Kūrma when blinking. Kṛkara should be known to create thirst. Devadatta is operational when yawning.
na jahāti mṛtaṃ cāpi sarvavyāpī dhanañjayaḥ |
ete nāḍīsahasreṣu vartante jīvarūpiṇaḥ ||34||

De-sandhi:
na jahāti mṛtam ca api sarva-vyāpī dhanañjayaḥ |
ete nāḍī-sahasreṣu vartante jīva-rūpiṇaḥ ||		 na = not
jahāti = leaves (3rd sg.)
mṛtam = dead [body] (acc.)
sarva-vyāpī = all-pervading (nom.)
dhanañjayaḥ = Dhanañjaya (nom.)
ete = these (nom. pl.)
nāḍī-sahasreṣu = in thousands of nāḍīs (loc. pl.)
vartante = exist (3rd pl. mid.)
jīva-rūpiṇaḥ = having form of life (nom. pl.)		 The all-pervading (sarvavyāpī) Dhanañjaya (dhanañjayaḥ) does not leave (na jahāti) even (api) the dead body (mṛtam). These [ten vāyus] (ete) exist (vartante) in the thousands of nāḍīs (nāḍīsahasreṣu), having the form of the vital principle (jīvarūpiṇaḥ). Dhanañjaya remains even after death
[√hā - to leave, √vṛt - to exist/dwell]		 Dhanañjaya is all-pervasive and does not leave even a dead [body]. These [breaths] exist in the thousands of channels in the form of the vital principle (jīva).
prāṇāpānavaśo jīvo adhaś ca ūrdhvaṃ pradhāvati |
vāmadakṣiṇamārgeṇa cañcalatvāt na dṛśyate ||35||

De-sandhi:
prāṇa-apāna-vaśaḥ jīvaḥ adhaḥ ca ūrdhvam pradhāvati |
vāma-dakṣiṇa-mārgeṇa cañcalatvāt na dṛśyate ||		 prāṇa-apāna-vaśaḥ = under control of prāṇa and apāna (nom.)
jīvaḥ = vital principle (nom.)
adhaḥ = down
ūrdhvam = up
pradhāvati = rushes (3rd sg.)
vāma-dakṣiṇa-mārgeṇa = through left and right paths (inst.)
cañcalatvāt = due to restlessness (abl.)
dṛśyate = is seen (pass.)		 The vital principle (jīvaḥ), under the control of prāṇa and apāna (prāṇāpānavaśaḥ), rushes (pradhāvati) downward and upward (adhaḥ ca ūrdhvam) through the left and right paths (vāmadakṣiṇamārgeṇa). Due to its restlessness (cañcalatvāt), it is not seen (na dṛśyate). Jīva rushes up and down via prāṇa-apāna
[√dhāv - to rush/run, √dṛś - to see]		 Under the control of prāṇa and apāna the vital principle rushes up and down through the left and right paths. It is so restless that it is imperceptible.
ākṣipto bhujadaṇḍena yathoccalati kandukaḥ |
prāṇāpānasamākṣiptaḥ tadvaj jīvo na viśramet ||36||

De-sandhi:
ākṣiptaḥ bhuja-daṇḍena yathā uccalati kandukaḥ |
prāṇa-apāna-samākṣiptaḥ tadvat jīvaḥ na viśramet ||		 ākṣiptaḥ = tossed (PPP, nom.)
bhuja-daṇḍena = by arm/stick (inst.)
yathā = as/like
uccalati = jumps (3rd sg.)
kandukaḥ = ball (nom.)
prāṇa-apāna-samākṣiptaḥ = tossed about by prāṇa and apāna (PPP, nom.)
tadvat = likewise
jīvaḥ = vital principle (nom.)
viśramet = rests (opt.)		 Just as (yathā) a ball (kandukaḥ) tossed (ākṣiptaḥ) by a stick (bhujadaṇḍena) jumps up (uccalati), likewise (tadvat) the vital principle (jīvaḥ), tossed about by prāṇa and apāna (prāṇāpānasamākṣiptaḥ), does not rest (na viśramet). Ball analogy: jīva tossed by prāṇa-apāna
[√kṣip - to throw/toss, √ut-cal - to jump, √vi-śram - to rest]		 In the same way that a ball jumps when hit by a stick, so the vital principle, tossed about by prāṇa and apāna, does not rest.
rajjubaddho yathā śyeno gato api ākṛṣyate punaḥ |
guṇabaddhaḥ tathā jīvaḥ prāṇāpānena kṛṣyate ||37||

De-sandhi:
rajju-baddhaḥ yathā śyenaḥ gataḥ api ākṛṣyate punaḥ |
guṇa-baddhaḥ tathā jīvaḥ prāṇa-apānena kṛṣyate ||		 rajju-baddhaḥ = tied by rope (BV, nom.)
yathā = as/like
śyenaḥ = hawk (nom.)
gataḥ = moved (PPP, nom.)
ākṛṣyate = is pulled back (pass.)
punaḥ = again
guṇa-baddhaḥ = bound by guṇas (BV, nom.)
tathā = likewise
jīvaḥ = vital principle (nom.)
prāṇa-apānena = by prāṇa and apāna (inst.)
kṛṣyate = is pulled (pass.)		 Just as (yathā) a hawk (śyenaḥ) bound by a rope (rajjubaddhaḥ), even though it has flown away (gataḥ api), is pulled back (ākṛṣyate punaḥ), likewise (tathā) the vital principle (jīvaḥ), bound by the guṇas (guṇabaddhaḥ), is pulled (kṛṣyate) by prāṇa and apāna (prāṇāpānena). Hawk analogy: jīva bound by guṇas
[√bandh - to bind, √gam - to go, √kṛṣ - to pull/draw]		 In the same way that a hawk tied by a rope is pulled back when it moves, so the vital principle bound by the guṇas is pulled by prāṇa and apāna.
apānaḥ karṣati prāṇam prāṇaḥ apānam ca karṣati |
khagarajjuvad iti etau yaḥ jānāti sa yogavit ||38||

De-sandhi:
apānaḥ karṣati prāṇam prāṇaḥ apānam ca karṣati |
khaga-rajju-vat iti etau yaḥ jānāti sa yoga-vit ||		 apānaḥ = Apāna (nom.)
karṣati = pulls (3rd sg.)
prāṇam = Prāṇa (acc.)
prāṇaḥ = Prāṇa (nom.)
apānam = Apāna (acc.)
ca = and
khaga-rajju-vat = like bird-rope (simile)
iti = thus
etau = these two (nom. du.)
yaḥ = who (rel. pron.)
jānāti = knows (3rd sg.)
sa = he (nom.)
yoga-vit = knower of yoga (nom.)		 Apāna (apānaḥ) pulls (karṣati) Prāṇa (prāṇam), and Prāṇa (prāṇaḥ) pulls (karṣati) Apāna (apānam). Thus (iti) these two (etau) are like a bird and rope (khagarajjuvat) — he who (yaḥ) knows (jānāti) this, he (sa) is a knower of yoga (yogavit). Prāṇa-apāna mutual relationship (bird-rope simile)
[√kṛṣ - to pull, √jñā - to know]		 Apāna pulls prāṇa and prāṇa pulls apāna. He who knows these two to be like a bird and a rope knows yoga.
hakāreṇa bahiryāti sakāreṇa viśetpunaḥ |
haṃsa haṃsa iti amum mantraṃ jīvaḥ japati sarvadā ||39||

De-sandhi:
ha-kāreṇa bahiḥ yāti sa-kāreṇa viśet punaḥ |
haṃsa haṃsa iti amum mantram jīvaḥ japati sarvadā ||		 ha-kāreṇa = with syllable 'ha' (inst.)
bahiḥ = out
yāti = goes (3rd sg.)
sa-kāreṇa = with syllable 'sa' (inst.)
viśet = enters (opt.)
punaḥ = again
haṃsa haṃsa = haṃsa haṃsa
iti = thus
amum = this (acc.)
mantram = mantra (acc.)
jīvaḥ = vital principle (nom.)
japati = repeats (3rd sg.)
sarvadā = always		 By the syllable 'ha' (hakāreṇa) it goes out (bahiryāti), by the syllable 'sa' (sakāreṇa) it enters (viśet) again (punaḥ). "Haṃsa haṃsa" (haṃsa haṃsa) — thus (iti) this (amum) mantra (mantram) the vital principle (jīvaḥ) repeats (japati) constantly (sarvadā). Haṃsa mantra of breath
[√yā - to go, √viś - to enter, √jap - to repeat]		 The vital principle goes out with the syllable ha [and] goes in and down with the syllable sa; it constantly repeats this mantra, haṃsa haṃsa.
ṣaṭśatāni divā rātrau sahasrāṇi ekaviṃśatiḥ |
etat saṅkhyānvitam mantram jīvaḥ japati sarvadā ||40||

De-sandhi:
ṣaṭ-śatāni divā rātrau sahasrāṇi eka-viṃśatiḥ |
etat saṅkhyā-anvitam mantram jīvaḥ japati sarvadā ||		 ṣaṭ-śatāni = six hundreds (nom. pl.)
divā = by day
rātrau = by night (loc.)
sahasrāṇi = thousands (nom. pl.)
eka-viṃśatiḥ = twenty-one (nom.)
etat = this (acc.)
saṅkhyā-anvitam = accompanied by number (acc.)
mantram = mantra (acc.)
jīvaḥ = vital principle (nom.)
japati = repeats (3rd sg.)
sarvadā = always		 Twenty-one (ekaviṃśatiḥ) thousand (sahasrāṇi) six hundred (ṣaṭśatāni) [times] by day and by night (divā rātrau) — this (etat) mantra (mantram) accompanied by [its] number (saṅkhyānvitam) the vital principle (jīvaḥ) constantly repeats (japati sarvadā). 21,600 daily breaths
[√jap - to repeat, √i - to go (anvitam)]		 The vital principle always repeats this mantra 21,600 times in a day and a night.
ajapā nāma gāyatrī yoginām mokṣadāyinī |
asyāḥ saṅkalpamātreṇa naraḥ pāpād vimucyate ||41||

De-sandhi:
ajapā nāma gāyatrī yoginām mokṣa-dāyinī |
asyāḥ saṅkalpa-mātreṇa naraḥ pāpāt vimucyate ||		 ajapā = Ajapā (nom.)
nāma = named
gāyatrī = Gāyatrī (nom.)
yoginām = of yogis (gen. pl.)
mokṣa-dāyinī = bestowing liberation (nom. fem.)
asyāḥ = of this (gen. fem.)
saṅkalpa-mātreṇa = by mere thought (inst.)
naraḥ = man (nom.)
pāpāt = from sin (abl.)
vimucyate = is freed (pass.)		 The Gāyatrī (gāyatrī) named (nāma) Ajapā (ajapā) is liberation-bestowing (mokṣadāyinī) for yogis (yoginām). By mere intention (saṅkalpamātreṇa) regarding this (asyāḥ), a person (naraḥ) is released (vimucyate) from sin (pāpāt). Ajapā Gāyatrī liberates
[√dā - to give, √muc - to release]		 [This], the Gāyatrī called Ajapā, bestows liberation upon yogis. Merely by thinking of it a man is freed from sin.
ajapāsadṛśī vidyā ajapāsadṛśaṃ tapaḥ |
ajapāsadṛśaṃ puṇyam na bhūtam na bhaviṣyati ||42||

De-sandhi:
ajapā-sadṛśī vidyā ajapā-sadṛśam tapaḥ |
ajapā-sadṛśam puṇyam na bhūtam na bhaviṣyati ||		 ajapā-sadṛśī = like Ajapā (nom. fem.)
vidyā = knowledge (nom.)
ajapā-sadṛśam = like Ajapā (nom. n.)
tapaḥ = austerity (nom.)
puṇyam = merit (nom.)
na = not
bhūtam = has been (PPP)
na = not
bhaviṣyati = will be (fut.)		 A knowledge (vidyā) similar to Ajapā (ajapāsadṛśī), an austerity (tapaḥ) similar to Ajapā (ajapāsadṛśam), a merit (puṇyam) similar to Ajapā (ajapāsadṛśam) — has not existed (na bhūtam) and will not exist (na bhaviṣyati). Supremacy of Ajapā
[√bhū - to be, √bhū (bhaviṣyati) - to become]		 There never has been nor never will be a mantra like Ajapā, an austerity like Ajapā or a meritorious action like Ajapā.
kuṇḍalinyāḥ samudbhūtā gāyatrī prāṇadhāriṇī |
praṇavādyā tathā vidyā yas tām vetti sa yogavit ||43||

De-sandhi:
kuṇḍalinyāḥ samudbhūtā gāyatrī prāṇa-dhāriṇī |
praṇava-ādyā tathā vidyā yaḥ tām vetti sa yoga-vit ||		 kuṇḍalinyāḥ = from Kuṇḍalinī (abl. fem.)
samudbhūtā = arisen (PPP, nom. fem.)
gāyatrī = Gāyatrī (nom.)
prāṇa-dhāriṇī = bearing prāṇa (nom. fem.)
praṇava-ādyā = beginning with Om (nom. fem.)
tathā = likewise
vidyā = knowledge/mantra (nom.)
yaḥ = who (rel. pron.)
tām = her (acc.)
vetti = knows (3rd sg.)
sa = he (nom.)
yoga-vit = knower of yoga (nom.)		 Gāyatrī (gāyatrī), having arisen (samudbhūtā) from Kuṇḍalinī (kuṇḍalinyāḥ), is prāṇa-bearing (prāṇadhāriṇī); and likewise (tathā) the knowledge (vidyā) beginning with Praṇava [Om] (praṇavādyā) — whoever (yaḥ) knows (vetti) her (tām), that one (sa) is a knower of yoga (yogavit). Gāyatrī from Kuṇḍalinī
[√bhū - to arise, √vid - to know, √dhṛ - to hold]		 And Gāyatrī, the mantra (vidyā) starting with Om, which bears Prāṇa, arises from Kuṇḍalinī. Who knows her knows yoga.
kandordhvaṃ kuṇḍalī śaktir aṣṭadhā kuṭilikṛtā |
brahmadvāramukhaṃ nityaṃ sukhena āvṛtya tiṣṭhati ||44||

De-sandhi:
kanda-ūrdhvam kuṇḍalī śaktiḥ aṣṭa-dhā kuṭilī-kṛtā |
brahma-dvāra-mukham nityam sukhena āvṛtya tiṣṭhati ||		 kanda-ūrdhvam = above the bulb
kuṇḍalī = Kuṇḍalinī (nom.)
śaktiḥ = power (nom.)
aṣṭa-dhā = eightfold
kuṭilī-kṛtā = made coiled (PPP)
brahma-dvāra-mukham = mouth of Brahman's door (acc.)
nityam = constantly
sukhena = with ease (inst.)
āvṛtya = covering (abs.)
tiṣṭhati = dwells (3rd sg.)		 Above the bulb (kandordhvam), the power (śaktiḥ) Kuṇḍalinī (kuṇḍalī), made coiled eightfold (aṣṭadhā kuṭilikṛtā), dwells (tiṣṭhati) constantly (nityam), having covered (āvṛtya) the opening of Brahman's door (brahmadvāramukham) comfortably (sukhena). Kuṇḍalinī location and posture
[√sthā - to stand/dwell, √vṛ - to cover]		 Above the Bulb is the Śakti Kuṇḍalinī which is coiled eight times and constantly dwells at ease covering the opening of the doorway of Brahman.
yena margeṇa gantavyaṃ brahmasthānam nirāmayam |
mukhenā āchādya tad dvāraṃ prasupta parameśvarī ||45||

De-sandhi:
yena margeṇa gantavyam brahma-sthānam nir-āmayam |
mukhena āchādya tat dvāram prasupta parama-īśvarī ||		 yena = by which (inst.)
margeṇa = by path (inst.)
gantavyam = to be gone (gerundive)
brahma-sthānam = place of Brahman (nom.)
nir-āmayam = disease-free (nom.)
mukhena = with mouth (inst.)
āchādya = covering (abs.)
tat = that (acc.)
dvāram = door (acc.)
prasupta = sleeping (PPP, nom. fem.)
parama-īśvarī = supreme goddess (nom.)		 By which (yena) path (margeṇa) one should go to (gantavyam) the disease-free (nirāmayam) abode of Brahman (brahmasthānam), that (tat) door (dvāram) the supreme goddess (parameśvarī), sleeping (prasupta), covers (āchādya) with her mouth (mukhena). Sleeping goddess guards door to Brahman
[√gam - to go, √chād - to cover, √svap - to sleep]		 The sleeping supreme goddess covers with her mouth the opening of the path by which the disease-free place of Brahman is to be reached.
prabuddhā vahniyogena manasā marutā saha |
śucīvad guṇam ādāya vrajaty ūrdhvaṃ suṣumṇayā ||46||

De-sandhi:
prabuddhā vahni-yogena manasā marutā saha |
śucī-vat guṇam ādāya vrajati ūrdhvam suṣumṇayā ||		 prabuddhā = awakened (PPP, nom. fem.)
vahni-yogena = by application of fire (inst.)
manasā = with mind (inst.)
marutā = with breath (inst.)
saha = together
śucī-vat = like a needle
guṇam = thread (acc.)
ādāya = taking (abs.)
vrajati = goes (3rd sg.)
ūrdhvam = upward
suṣumṇayā = by Suṣumṇā (inst.)		 When awakened (prabuddhā) by union with fire (vahniyogena), together with (saha) the mind (manasā) and the breath (marutā), like a needle (śucīvat) taking (ādāya) a thread (guṇam), she goes (vrajati) upward (ūrdhvam) through Suṣumṇā (suṣumṇayā). Awakening Kuṇḍalinī (needle-thread simile)
[√budh - to awaken, √vraj - to go, √ā-dā - to take]		 Awakened by the application of fire, together with the mind [and] the breath, she goes upwards along the Suṣumṇā like a needle taking a thread.
prasphuradbhujagākārā padmatantunubhā śubhā |
prabuddhā vahniyogena vrajaty ūrdhvam suṣumṇayā ||47||

De-sandhi:
prasphurat-bhujaga-ākārā padma-tantu-nibhā śubhā |
prabuddhā vahni-yogena vrajati ūrdhvam suṣumṇayā ||		 prasphurat-bhujaga-ākārā = having form of glistening snake (nom. fem.)
padma-tantu-nibhā = resembling lotus thread (nom. fem.)
śubhā = goodly/auspicious (nom. fem.)
prabuddhā = awakened (PPP, nom. fem.)
vahni-yogena = by application of fire (inst.)
vrajati = goes (3rd sg.)
ūrdhvam = upward
suṣumṇayā = by Suṣumṇā (inst.)		 Having the appearance (ākārā) of a shimmering (prasphurat) serpent (bhujaga), resembling (nibhā) a lotus filament (padmatantu), the auspicious one (śubhā), awakened (prabuddhā) by union with fire (vahniyogena), travels (vrajati) upward (ūrdhvam) through Suṣumṇā (suṣumṇayā). Kuṇḍalinī appearance
[√sphur - to shimmer, √vraj - to go, √budh - to awaken]		 Having the form of a glistening snake [and] resembling a lotus thread, the goodly [Kuṇḍalinī], awakened by the application of fire, goes upwards along the Suṣumṇā.
uddhaṭayet kapāṭaṃ tu yathā kuñcikayā haṭhāt |
kuṇḍalinyā tathā mokṣadvāram vibhedayet ||48||

De-sandhi:
uddhaṭayet kapāṭam tu yathā kuñcikayā haṭhāt |
kuṇḍalinyā tathā mokṣa-dvāram vibhedayet ||		 uddhaṭayet = one might open (opt.)
kapāṭam = door (acc.)
tu = indeed
yathā = as/just as
kuñcikayā = with key (inst.)
haṭhāt = by force
kuṇḍalinyā = with Kuṇḍalinī (inst.)
tathā = so/likewise
mokṣa-dvāram = door to liberation (acc.)
vibhedayet = should break open (opt.)		 Just as (yathā) one might forcibly open (uddhaṭayet haṭhāt) a bolt (kapāṭam) with a key (kuñcikayā), similarly (tathā) one should pierce open (vibhedayet) the door of liberation (mokṣadvāram) with Kuṇḍalinī (kuṇḍalinyā). Opening liberation's door (key analogy)
[√haṭ - to open forcibly, √bhid - to pierce/break]		 In the same way that one might compel a door to open using a key, so does the yogi break open the doorway to liberation using Kuṇḍalinī.
kandordhvaṃ kuṇḍalī śaktiḥ suptā mokṣāya yoginām |
bandhanāya ca mūḍhānāṃ yas tāṃ vetti sa yogavit ||49||

De-sandhi:
kanda-ūrdhvam kuṇḍalī śaktiḥ suptā mokṣāya yoginām |
bandhanāya ca mūḍhānām yaḥ tām vetti sa yoga-vit ||		 kanda-ūrdhvam = above the bulb
kuṇḍalī = Kuṇḍalinī (nom.)
śaktiḥ = power (nom.)
suptā = sleeping (PPP, nom. fem.)
mokṣāya = for liberation (dat.)
yoginām = of yogis (gen. pl.)
bandhanāya = for bondage (dat.)
ca = and
mūḍhānām = of fools (gen. pl.)
yaḥ = who (rel. pron.)
tām = her (acc.)
vetti = knows (3rd sg.)
sa = he (nom.)
yoga-vit = knower of yoga (nom.)		 Above the bulb (kandordhvam), the power (śaktiḥ) Kuṇḍalinī (kuṇḍalī), sleeping (suptā), [exists] for the liberation (mokṣāya) of yogis (yoginām), and (ca) for the bondage (bandhanāya) of the confused (mūḍhānām). Whoever (yaḥ) knows (vetti) her (tām), that one (sa) is a knower of yoga (yogavit). Kuṇḍalinī for liberation or bondage
[√svap - to sleep, √vid - to know, √bandh - to bind]		 The Śakti Kuṇḍalinī who sleeps above the Bulb leads to liberation for yogis and bondage for fools. Who knows her knows yoga.
kṛtvā sampuṭitau karau dṛḍhataraṃ baddhvā atha padmāsanam
gāḍhaṃ vakṣasi sannidhāya cibukaṃ dhyāyaṃś ca tad cetasi |
vāraṃ vāram apānam ūrdhvam anilaṃ proccālayan pūritam
muñcan prāṇam upaiti bodham atulam śaktiprabhāvān naraḥ ||50||

De-sandhi:
kṛtvā sampuṭitau karau dṛḍha-taram baddhvā atha padma-āsanam
gāḍham vakṣasi sannidhāya cibukam dhyāyan ca tat cetasi |
vāram vāram apānam ūrdhvam anilam proccālayan pūritam
muñcan prāṇam upaiti bodham atulam śakti-prabhāvāt naraḥ ||		 kṛtvā = having made (abs.)
sampuṭitau = cupped together (acc. du.)
karau = hands (acc. du.)
dṛḍha-taram = very firmly (adv.)
baddhvā = having bound (abs.)
atha = then
padma-āsanam = lotus posture (acc.)
gāḍham = firmly
vakṣasi = on chest (loc.)
sannidhāya = placing (abs.)
cibukam = chin (acc.)
dhyāyan = meditating (pres. part.)
tat = on that
cetasi = in mind (loc.)
vāram vāram = again and again
apānam = Apāna (acc.)
ūrdhvam = upward
anilam = breath (acc.)
proccālayan = raising up (causative pres. part.)
pūritam = filled (PPP, acc.)
muñcan = releasing (pres. part.)
prāṇam = Prāṇa (acc.)
upaiti = attains (3rd sg.)
bodham = knowledge (acc.)
atulam = incomparable (acc.)
śakti-prabhāvāt = from power of Śakti (abl.)
naraḥ = man (nom.)		 Having made (kṛtvā) the two hands (karau) joined together (sampuṭitau), having very firmly bound (dṛḍhataram baddhvā) the lotus posture (padmāsanam), firmly (gāḍham) placing (sannidhāya) the chin (cibukam) on the chest (vakṣasi), and meditating (dhyāyan) on that (tat) in the heart (cetasi), repeatedly (vāraṃ vāram) driving upward (proccālayan ūrdhvam) Apāna (apānam) — the vital air (anilam) being filled (pūritam) — releasing (muñcan) Prāṇa (prāṇam), a person (naraḥ) attains (upaiti) incomparable (atulam) awakening (bodham) from the power of Śakti (śaktiprabhāvāt). Mahāmudrā technique
[√kṛ - to do, √bandh - to bind, √dhyai - to meditate, √muc - to release, √i - to attain]		 Having cupped the hands together and bound the lotus posture very firmly, firmly placing the chin on the chest and meditating on that in the mind, again and again raising Apāna upward, the breath filled, releasing Prāṇa, a man attains incomparable knowledge from the power of Śakti.
aṅgānāṃ mardanaṃ kṛtvā śramasaṃjātavāriṇā |
kaṭvāmlalavaṇatyāgī bhūtvā bhojanam ācaret ||51||

De-sandhi:
aṅgānām mardanam kṛtvā śrama-saṃjāta-vāriṇā |
kaṭu-āmla-lavaṇa-tyāgī bhūtvā bhojanam ācaret ||		 aṅgānām = of limbs (gen. pl.)
mardanam = rubbing/massage (acc.)
kṛtvā = having done (abs.)
śrama-saṃjāta-vāriṇā = with water born of exertion (inst.)
kaṭu-āmla-lavaṇa-tyāgī = abandoning pungent, sour, salty (nom.)
bhūtvā = having become (abs.)
bhojanam = food (acc.)
ācaret = should take (opt.)		 After having rubbed (mardanam kṛtvā) the limbs (aṅgānām) with sweat—water produced from exertion (śramasaṃjātavāriṇā)—and having become (bhūtvā) one who rejects (tyāgī) the pungent, sour, and salty (kaṭvāmlalavaṇa), one should consume (ācaret) food (bhojanam). Post-practice care and diet
[√mṛd - to rub/massage, √kṛ - to do, √tyaj - to abandon, √car - to practice]		 Having massaged the limbs with water born of exertion [sweat], having abandoned pungent, sour and salty [foods], one should take food.
brahmacārī mitāhārī yogī yogaparāyaṇaḥ |
abdād ūrdhvaṃ bhavet siddho nātra kāryā vicāraṇā ||52||

De-sandhi:
brahmacārī mita-āhārī yogī yoga-parāyaṇaḥ |
abdāt ūrdhvam bhavet siddhaḥ na atra kāryā vicāraṇā ||		 brahmacārī = celibate (nom.)
mita-āhārī = moderate eater (nom.)
yogī = yogi (nom.)
yoga-parāyaṇaḥ = devoted to yoga (nom.)
abdāt = from year (abl.)
ūrdhvam = after
bhavet = becomes (opt.)
siddhaḥ = perfected (nom.)
na = not
atra = here
kāryā = to be done
vicāraṇā = inquiry (nom.)		 The yogi (yogī) who practices celibacy (brahmacārī), eats moderately (mitāhārī), and is completely devoted to yoga (yogaparāyaṇaḥ) will become (bhavet) accomplished (siddhaḥ) within a year (abdād ūrdhvam). Here (atra), no (na) further deliberation (vicāraṇā) need be undertaken (kāryā). Brahmacarī practices: perfection in one year
[√bhū - to become, √sidh - to accomplish]		 A celibate, moderate eater, yogi devoted to yoga becomes perfected after a year — no inquiry should be made about this.
susnigdhaṃ madhurāhāram caturthāmśavivarjitam
bhuñhate surasamprītyai mitāhārī sa ucyate

De-sandhi:
su-snigdham madhura-āhāram caturtha-aṃśa-vivarjitam
bhuñhate sura-samprītyai mita-āhārī saḥ ucyate		 su-snigdham = very unctuous/pleasant (acc. sg. n.)
madhura-āhāram = sweet food (acc. sg.)
caturtha-aṃśa-vivarjitam = leaving fourth part aside (acc. sg.)
bhuñhate = eats (3rd sg. mid.)
sura-samprītyai = for gods' satisfaction (dat.)
mita-āhārī = moderate eater (nom. sg.)
saḥ = he (nom.)
ucyate = is called (3rd sg. pass.)		 He who eats (bhuñhate) very unctuous (susnigdham), sweet food (madhurāhāram), leaving aside the fourth part (caturthāmśavivarjitam), in order to please (samprītyai) the gods (sura)—he (saḥ) is called (ucyate) a moderate eater (mitāhārī). Definition of mitāhāra (moderate eating)
[√bhuj - to eat, √vac - to call, √vṛj - to abandon]
Eating pleasant food while leaving 1/4 of stomach empty.		 He who, in order to please the gods, eats unctuous, sweet food leaving aside a quarter of it is said to be one who has a restricted diet.
kandordhaṃ kuṇḍalī śakriḥ suptā mokṣāya yoginām
banshanāya ca mūḍānām yastāṃ vetti sa yogavit

De-sandhi:
kanda-ūrdhvam kuṇḍalī śakriḥ suptā mokṣāya yoginām
banshanāya ca mūḍānām yaḥ tām vetti saḥ yoga-vit		 kanda-ūrdhvam = above the bulb (adv.)
kuṇḍalī = coiled (nom. sg. f.)
śakriḥ = Śakti/power (nom. sg.)
suptā = sleeping (nom. sg. f.)
mokṣāya = for liberation (dat.)
yoginām = of yogis (gen. pl.)
banshanāya = for bondage (dat.)
ca = and
mūḍānām = of fools (gen. pl.)
yaḥ = who (nom.)
tām = her (acc.)
vetti = knows (3rd sg.)
saḥ = he (nom.)
yoga-vit = knower of yoga (nom.)		 Above the kanda-bulb (kandordhvam) the coiled (kuṇḍalī) Śakti (śakriḥ) lies sleeping (suptā), for the liberation (mokṣāya) of yogis (yoginām) and (ca) for the bondage (banshanāya) of fools (mūḍānām). Who (yaḥ) knows (vetti) her (tām), he (saḥ) [is] a knower of yoga (yogavit). Kuṇḍalinī: liberation or bondage
[√vid - to know]
The coiled Śakti brings liberation to yogis who know her, bondage to fools who don't.		 The coiled goddess sleeps above the bulb for the liberation of yogis. Because it binds bondage it is called a lock.
MUDRĀBANDHĀḤ (SEALS AND LOCKS)
mahāmudṛām nabhomudrāmuddīyāṇam jalandharam
mūlabandhaṃ ca yo vetti sa yogī muktibhājanam

De-sandhi:
mahā-mudṛām nabha-mudrām uḍḍīyāṇam jalandharam
mūla-bandham ca yaḥ vetti saḥ yogī mukti-bhājanam		 mahā-mudrām = great seal (acc. sg. f.)
nabha-mudrām = sky seal (acc. sg. f.)
uḍḍīyāṇam = uḍḍīyāṇa (acc. sg. n.)
jalandharam = jālandhara (acc. sg. n.)
mūla-bandham = root lock (acc.)
ca = and
yaḥ = who (nom.)
vetti = knows (3rd sg.)
saḥ = he (nom.)
yogī = yogi (nom.)
mukti-bhājanam = vessel/receptacle of liberation (nom. sg. n.)		 Whoever (yaḥ) knows (vetti) mahāmudrā (mahāmudrām), nabhomudrā (nabhomudrām), uḍḍīyāṇa (uḍḍīyāṇam), jālandhara (jalandharam), and (ca) mūlabandha (mūlabandham)—that (saḥ) yogi (yogī) [is] a vessel of liberation (muktibhājanam). List of the five main mudrās/bandhas
[√vid - to know, √bhaj - to partake/share]
Enumeration of the essential practices. The yogi becomes a receptacle/vessel (bhājana) for liberation.		 The yogi who knows the great seal, the sky seal, uḍḍīyāna, jālandhara and the root lock becomes a sharer of perfections.
apānaprāṇayoraikyam kṣayo mūtrapurīṣayoḥ
yuvā bhvati vṛddho api satatam mūlabandhanāt

De-sandhi:
apāna-prāṇayoḥ aikyam kṣayaḥ mūtra-purīṣayoḥ
yuvā bhavati vṛddhaḥ api satatam mūla-bandhanāt		 apāna-prāṇayoḥ = of apāna and prāṇa (gen. dual)
aikyam = unity (nom. sg.)
kṣayaḥ = decrease (nom.)
mūtra-purīṣayoḥ = of urine and feces (gen. dual)
yuvā = youth (nom.)
bhavati = becomes (3rd sg.)
vṛddhaḥ = old man (nom.)
api = even
satatam = constantly (adv.)
mūla-bandhanāt = from root lock (abl.)		 Unity (aikyam) of apāna and prāṇa (apānaprāṇayoḥ), reduction (kṣayaḥ) of urine and feces (mūtrapurīṣayoḥ)—even (api) an old person (vṛddhaḥ) becomes (bhavati) youthful (yuvā) by constant (satatam) [practice of] mūlabandha (mūlabandhanāt). Benefits of mūlabandha
[√bhū - to become, √kṣi - to diminish]
Uniting the two main breaths and rejuvenation.		 Through constantly [practicing] the root lock there is unity of apāna and prāṇa and a decrease in urine and feces. Even an old man becomes young.
pārṣṇibhāgena sampīḍya yonimākuṇcyed gudam
apānamūrdhvamākṛṣya mulabandho ayamucyate

De-sandhi:
pārṣṇi-bhāgena sampīḍya yonim ākuñcyet gudam
apānam ūrdhvam ākṛṣya mūla-bandhaḥ ayam ucyate		 pārṣṇi-bhāgena = with heel part (inst.)
sampīḍya = pressing (abs.)
yonim = perineum (acc.)
ākuñcyet = should contract (3rd sg. opt.)
gudam = anus (acc.)
apānam = apāna breath (acc.)
ūrdhvam = upward (adv.)
ākṛṣya = drawing (abs.)
mūla-bandhaḥ = root lock (nom.)
ayam = this (nom.)
ucyate = is called (3rd sg. pass.)		 Having pressed (sampīḍya) the perineum (yonim) with the heel-part (pārṣṇibhāgena), one should contract (ākuñcyet) the anus (gudam), drawing (ākṛṣya) apāna (apānam) upward (ūrdhvam). This (ayam) is called (ucyate) 'mūlabandha' (mūlabandhaḥ). Technique of mūlabandha
[√pīḍ - to press, √kuñc - to contract, √kṛṣ - to draw, √vac - to call]
Press perineum with heel, contract anus, draw apāna upward.		 Pressing the perineum with the heel, one should draw the breath together and make an upward contraction. This is known by the name root lock.
uddīṇam kurute yasmād aviśrāntaṃ mahākhagaḥ
uddiyānaṃ tadeva syātttra bandho vidhīyate

De-sandhi:
uḍḍīyanam kurute yasmāt aviśrāntam mahā-khagaḥ
uḍḍiyānam tat eva syāt tatra bandhaḥ vidhīyate		 uḍḍīyanam = upward flight (acc.)
kurute = makes/does (3rd sg. mid.)
yasmāt = because (abl.)
aviśrāntam = unceasingly, without rest (adv.)
mahā-khagaḥ = great bird (nom.)
uḍḍiyānam = uḍḍīyāna (nom.)
tat = that (nom. n.)
eva = indeed
syāt = should be (3rd sg. opt.)
tatra = there
bandhaḥ = lock (nom.)
vidhīyate = is prescribed (3rd sg. pass.)		 Because (yasmāt) the great bird (mahākhagaḥ) performs (kurute) upward flight (uḍḍīyanam) unceasingly (aviśrāntam), that (tat) indeed (eva) would be (syāt) 'uḍḍīyāna' (uḍḍiyānam). There (tatra) the bandha (bandhaḥ) is prescribed (vidhīyate). Etymology of uḍḍīyāna
[√kṛ - to make, √as - to be, √vidhā - to prescribe]
Named after the great bird (khaga) that flies upward without ceasing.		 Because the great bird makes upward flight unceasingly, that indeed should be uḍḍīyāna. There the lock is prescribed.
udare paścime tāṇam nābherūrdhvaṃ ca kārayet
uddiyāno hyasau bandho mṛtyumātaṇgakesarī

De-sandhi:
udare paścime tāṇam nābheḥ ūrdhvam ca kārayet
uḍḍiyānaḥ hi asau bandhaḥ mṛtyu-mātaṇga-kesarī		 udare = in belly (loc.)
paścime = posterior (loc.)
tāṇam = stretching (acc.)
nābheḥ = of navel (gen.)
ūrdhvam = upward (adv.)
ca = and
kārayet = should make (3rd sg. caus. opt.)
uḍḍiyānaḥ = uḍḍīyāna (nom.)
hi = indeed
asau = that (nom.)
bandhaḥ = lock (nom.)
mṛtyu-mātaṇga-kesarī = lion to the elephant of death (nom.)		 One should cause (kārayet) stretching (tāṇam) of the belly (udare) backwards (paścime) and (ca) upwards (ūrdhvam) from the navel (nābheḥ). That (asau) uḍḍīyāna-bandha (uḍḍiyānaḥ bandhaḥ) indeed (hi) [is] a lion (kesarī) to the elephant (mātaṇga) of death (mṛtyu). Technique and metaphor of uḍḍīyāna
[√kṛ - to make]
Drawing the belly back and up; like a lion killing the elephant of death.		 One should make the belly stretch back and upward from the navel. The knower of yoga conquers death in six months through uḍḍīyāna.
badhnāti hi śirājālamadhogāminabhojalam
tataḥ jālandharo bandhḥ kaṇṭhaduḥkhaudhanāśanaḥ

De-sandhi:
badhnāti hi śirā-jālam adhaḥ-gāmi nabhaḥ-jalam
tataḥ jālandharaḥ bandhaḥ kaṇṭha-duḥkha-udha-nāśanaḥ		 badhnāti = binds (3rd sg.)
hi = indeed
śirā-jālam = network of channels (acc.)
adhaḥ-gāmi = going downward (acc.)
nabhaḥ-jalam = sky-water/nectar (acc.)
tataḥ = therefore
jālandharaḥ = jālandhara (nom.)
bandhaḥ = lock (nom.)
kaṇṭha-duḥkha-udha-nāśanaḥ = destroyer of throat suffering (nom.)		 Indeed (hi) it binds (badhnāti) the network of channels (śirājālam), the downward-flowing (adhogāmi) sky-nectar (nabhojalam). Therefore (tataḥ) jālandhara-bandha (jālandharaḥ bandhaḥ) [is] the destroyer (nāśanaḥ) of throat-suffering (kaṇṭhaduḥkha). Function and benefit of jālandhara
[√bandh - to bind, √naś - to destroy]
Binds the downward flow of nectar; removes throat pain.		 Indeed it binds the network of channels going downward to the navel cavity. Therefore it is called jālandhara—the throat contraction sequence.
jālandhare kṛte bandhe kaṇṭhasaṃkocalakṣaṇe
na pīyūṣaṃ pataryagnau na ca vāyuḥ pradhāvati

De-sandhi:
jālandhare kṛte bandhe kaṇṭha-saṃkoca-lakṣaṇe
na pīyūṣam patati agnau na ca vāyuḥ pradhāvati		 jālandhare = jālandhara (loc.)
kṛte = done (loc.)
bandhe = lock (loc.)
kaṇṭha-saṃkoca-lakṣaṇe = characterized by throat contraction (loc.)
na = not
pīyūṣam = nectar (nom.)
patati = falls (3rd sg.)
agnau = in fire (loc.)
na ca = and not
vāyuḥ = breath (nom.)
pradhāvati = runs forth (3rd sg.)		 When jālandhara-bandha (jālandhare bandhe) is made (kṛte), characterized by throat-contraction (kaṇṭhasaṃkocalakṣaṇe), the nectar (pīyūṣam) does not (na) fall (patati) into the fire (agnau), and (ca) the vāyu (vāyuḥ) does not run forth (pradhāvati). Effects of jālandhara
[√kṛ - to do, √pat - to fall, √dhāv - to run]
Preserves the nectar from falling into fire; restrains breath.		 When the jālandhara lock is done, characterized by throat contraction, the nectar does not fall into the fire and the breath does not become agitated.
kapālakuhare jihvā praviṣṭā viparītagā
bhruvorantargatā dṛṣṭirmudrābhavati khecarī

De-sandhi:
kapāla-kuhare jihvā praviṣṭā viparīta-gā
bhruvoḥ-antara-gatā dṛṣṭiḥ mudrā bhavati khecarī		 kapāla-kuhare = in skull cavity (loc.)
jihvā = tongue (nom.)
praviṣṭā = entered (nom. f.)
viparīta-gā = gone backwards (nom. f.)
bhruvoḥ-antara-gatā = gone between eyebrows (nom. f.)
dṛṣṭiḥ = gaze (nom.)
mudrā = seal (nom.)
bhavati = becomes (3rd sg.)
khecarī = sky-moving (nom. f.)		 The tongue (jihvā) having entered (praviṣṭā) the skull-cavity (kapālakuhare), gone backwards (viparītagā), the gaze (dṛṣṭiḥ) gone (gatā) between the eyebrows (bhruvorantara)—the mudrā (mudrā) becomes (bhavati) khecarī (khecarī). Description of khecarī mudrā
[√viś - to enter, √gam - to go, √bhū - to become]
Tongue turned back into skull with upward gaze.		 The tongue turned back and entered into the hollow of the skull, the gaze between the brows: this is khecarī mudrā.
na rogo maraṇaṃ tandrā na nidrā na kṣudhā tṛṣā
na ca mūrcchā bhavettasya yo mudrāṃ vetti khecarīm

De-sandhi:
na rogaḥ maraṇam tandrā na nidrā na kṣudhā tṛṣā
na ca mūrcchā bhavet tasya yaḥ mudrām vetti khecarīm		 na = not
rogaḥ = disease (nom.)
maraṇam = death (nom.)
tandrā = torpor (nom.)
na nidrā = not sleep (nom.)
na kṣudhā = not hunger (nom.)
tṛṣā = thirst (nom.)
na ca mūrcchā = and not fainting (nom.)
bhavet = occurs (3rd sg. opt.)
tasya = of him (gen.)
yaḥ = who (nom.)
mudrām = seal (acc.)
vetti = knows (3rd sg.)
khecarīm = sky-moving (acc. f.)		 Neither disease (rogaḥ), death (maraṇam), torpor (tandrā), nor (na) sleep (nidrā), nor hunger (kṣudhā), thirst (tṛṣā), and nor (na ca) fainting (mūrcchā) would occur (bhavet) for him (tasya) who (yaḥ) knows (vetti) the khecarī mudrā (khecarīm mudrām). Benefits of khecarī mudrā (1)
[√bhū - to be/become]
Freedom from disease, death, and bodily needs.		 No disease, death, torpor, sleep, hunger, thirst, or fainting occurs to the embodied one [who practices] khecarī mudrā.
pīḍyate na sarogeṇa lipyate na ca karmaṇā
bādhyate na sa kālena yo mudrāṃ vetti khecarim

De-sandhi:
pīḍyate na sa rogeṇa lipyate na ca karmaṇā
bādhyate na sa kālena yaḥ mudrām vetti khecarim		 pīḍyate = is afflicted (3rd sg. pass.)
na sa = not he
rogeṇa = by disease (inst.)
lipyate = is stained (3rd sg. pass.)
na ca = and not
karmaṇā = by karma (inst.)
bādhyate = is troubled (3rd sg. pass.)
na sa = not he
kālena = by time (inst.)
yaḥ = who (nom.)
mudrām = seal (acc.)
vetti = knows (3rd sg.)
khecarim = sky-moving (acc. f.)		 He (sa) is not (na) afflicted (pīḍyate) by disease (rogeṇa), not (na) stained (lipyate) by karma (karmaṇā), and (ca) not oppressed (bādhyate) by time (kālena)—who (yaḥ) knows (vetti) the khecarī mudrā (khecarim mudrām). Benefits of khecarī mudrā (2)
[√pīḍ - to afflict, √lip - to smear, √bādh - to trouble]
Transcending disease, karma, and time.		 He is not afflicted by disease, not stained by karma, and not troubled by time—those by whom the seal is practiced.
cittam carati khe yasmājjihvā carati khe gatā
tenaiṣā khecarī nāma mudrā siddhairnamaskṛta

De-sandhi:
cittam carati khe yasmāt jihvā carati khe gatā
tena eṣā khecarī nāma mudrā siddhaiḥ namaskṛta		 cittam = mind (nom.)
carati = moves (3rd sg.)
khe = in space (loc.)
yasmāt = because (abl.)
jihvā = tongue (nom.)
carati = moves (3rd sg.)
khe = in space (loc.)
gatā = gone (nom. f.)
tena = therefore (inst.)
eṣā = this (nom. f.)
khecarī = space-moving (nom.)
nāma = by name
mudrā = seal (nom.)
siddhaiḥ = by perfected ones (inst. pl.)
namaskṛta = honored/saluted (nom. f.)		 Because (yasmāt) the mind (cittam) moves (carati) in space (khe) and the tongue (jihvā), having gone (gatā), moves (carati) in space (khe), therefore (tena) this (eṣā) mudrā (mudrā) is honored (namaskṛta) by the siddhas (siddhaiḥ) with the name (nāma) 'khecarī' (khecarī). Etymology of khecarī
[√car - to move, √gam - to go, √namas - to honor]
Both mind and tongue move in the space (kha) of consciousness.		 Because the mind moves in space and the tongue, having gone, moves in space, therefore this seal is shown by the perfected ones with the name khecarī.
bindumūlaṃ śariram tu sirāstatra pratiṣṭhitāḥ
plāvayanti śarirem yā āpādatalamastakam

De-sandhi:
bindu-mūlam śarīram tu sirāḥ tatra pratiṣṭhitāḥ
plāvayanti śarīram yāḥ ā-pāda-tala-mastakam		 bindu-mūlam = root in bindu (nom. n.)
śarīram = body (nom.)
tu = but/indeed
sirāḥ = channels (nom. pl.)
tatra = there
pratiṣṭhitāḥ = established (nom. pl. f.)
plāvayanti = cause to float/fill (3rd pl.)
śarīram = body (acc.)
yāḥ = which (nom. pl. f.)
ā-pāda-tala-mastakam = from sole of foot to head (acc.)		 The body (śarīram) indeed (tu) has bindu as its root (bindumūlam). There (tatra) the channels (sirāḥ) are established (pratiṣṭhitāḥ), which (yāḥ) fill (plāvayanti) the body (śarīram) from the sole of the foot to the head (āpādatalamastakam). Bindu as foundation and channels
[√sthā - to stand, √plu - to float]
Body rooted in bindu; channels established there fill the entire body.		 The body has its root in bindu and exists in the places of bindu. As long as bindu is steady in the body, so long there is attachment to the body.
khecaryā mudrāṃ yena vivaram lambhikordhvataḥ
na tasya kṣarate binduḥ kāminyāliṅgitasya ca

De-sandhi:
khecaryā mudrām yena vivaram lambhikā ūrdhvataḥ
na tasya kṣarate binduḥ kāminyā āliṅgitasya ca		 khecaryā = by khecarī (inst.)
mudrām = seal (acc.)
yena = by which (inst.)
vivaram = opening/cavity (acc.)
lambhikā = uvula (nom.)
ūrdhvataḥ = from above
na = not
tasya = of him (gen.)
kṣarate = flows/drips (3rd sg.)
binduḥ = drop (nom.)
kāminyā = by woman (inst.)
āliṅgitasya = of embraced one (gen.)
ca = and		 By the khecarīmudrā (khecaryā mudrām), through which (yena) [the tongue reaches] the opening (vivaram) above (ūrdhvataḥ) the uvula (lambhikā), of him (tasya) bindu (binduḥ) does not (na) drip (kṣarate), even (ca) when embraced (āliṅgitasya) by a woman (kāminyā). Khecarī preserves bindu even in passion
[√kṣar - to flow/drip, √liṅg - to embrace]
Tongue reaching cavity above uvula prevents loss of vital essence.		 By khecarī mudrā the bindu does not fall anywhere—even the bindu that has fallen from the moon, having gone to the cavity of khecarī.
