Upaniṣads - Scholarly Analysis

Selected passages with detailed linguistic and philosophical analysis

Bṛhadāraṇyaka Upaniṣad
Śvetāśvatara Upaniṣad

Bṛhadāraṇyaka Upaniṣad 1.5.2-3

With Śaṅkara's Commentary (Bhāṣya) - The Seven Foods

Sanskrit Text Word-by-Word Analysis Literal Translation Grammar/Commentary Key Terms
BṚHADĀRAṆYAKA 1.5.2 - ŚAṄKARA'S COMMENTARY ON THE SEVEN FOODS
'yat saptānnāni medhayā
tapasā janayat pitā' iti
medhayā hi tapasā janayat pitā		 • yat = that which (rel. pron.)
• sapta-annāni = seven foods
• medhayā = through meditation, wisdom (inst. f. from medhā)
• tapasā = through austerity (inst. n. from tapas)
• janayat (ajanayat) = created (3sg. imperf. caus. from √jan)
• pitā = Father, Prajāpati (nom. m.)
• iti = thus (quotative)
• hi = indeed, for (emphatic particle) 		[Regarding] "That (yat) the Father (pitā) created (janayat) seven foods (saptānnāni) through wisdom (medhayā) and austerity (tapasā)" - indeed (hi) the Father (pitā) created (janayat) [them] through meditation (medhayā) and austerity (tapasā). Śaṅkara quotes the Upaniṣadic verse and affirms it. The dual means (medhā + tapas) are necessary for creation. Standard bhāṣya format: quote then explain. medhā - mental vigor, wisdom
tapas - heat, austerity
√jan (caus.) - to generate
Bhāṣya structure
THE COMMON FOOD
'ekamasya sādhāraṇam' iti
idam eva asya tat sādhāraṇam annam
yad idam adyate		 • ekam = one (nom./acc. n.)
• asya = of this/his (gen.)
• sādhāraṇam = common, shared (adj. from sā-dhāraṇa)
• idam = this (nom./acc. n.)
• eva = indeed, exactly (particle)
• tat = that (nom./acc. n.)
• annam = food
• yat = which (relative)
• adyate = is eaten (3sg. pres. pass. from √ad) 		[Regarding] "One (ekam) of these (asya) is common (sādhāraṇam)" - this (idam) very (eva) [food] that (yat) is eaten (adyate) is that (tat) common (sādhāraṇam) food (annam) of his (asya). First food identified: the common food (sādhāraṇam) shared by all. This is ordinary food that everyone eats. √dhṛ with sa- prefix = "held in common". sādhāraṇa - held in common
√ad - to eat
√dhṛ - to hold
Common sustenance
sa ya etad upāste
na sa pāpmano vyāvartate
miśraṃ hy etat		 • saḥ = he (nom. m.)
• yaḥ = who (nom. m. relative)
• etat = this (acc. n.)
• upāste = worships, meditates upon (3sg. pres. mid. from upa-√ās)
• na = not
• pāpmanaḥ = from evil, sin (abl. m. from pāpman)
• vyāvartate = turns away (3sg. pres. mid. from vi-ā-√vṛt)
• miśram = mixed, impure (PPP from √miś)
• hy (hi) = for, indeed 		He (saḥ) who (yaḥ) worships (upāste) this (etat) does not (na) turn away (vyāvartate) from evil (pāpmanaḥ), for (hi) this (etat) is mixed (miśram). Warning: worshipping the common food doesn't purify because it's miśra (mixed/impure). This food is morally neutral - both good and bad partake. √vṛt with vi-ā- = "to turn completely away from". upa-√ās - to sit near, worship
pāpman - evil, sin
vi-ā-√vṛt - to turn away
√miś - to mix
Mixed nature
TWO FOODS FOR THE GODS
'dve devān abhājayat' iti
hutaṃ ca prahutaṃ ca		 • dve = two (nom./acc. n. dual)
• devān = to the gods (acc. pl. m.)
• abhājayat = distributed, apportioned (3sg. imperf. caus. from ā-√bhaj)
• iti = thus
• hutam = oblation, what is offered in fire (PPP from √hu)
• ca = and
• prahutam = offering, present (PPP from pra-√hu) 		[Regarding] "Two (dve) he apportioned (abhājayat) to the gods (devān)" - [these are] the oblation (hutam) and (ca) the offering (prahutam). Two foods for gods: huta (burnt oblation in fire) and prahuta (offered food/gifts). √bhaj with ā- = "to distribute, apportion". Both are sacrificial offerings but different types. √bhaj - to share, divide
√hu - to offer in fire
pra-√hu - to offer forth
Two types of sacrifice
tasmād devebhyo juhvati ca
pra ca juhvanti		 • tasmāt = therefore (abl. from tat)
• devebhyaḥ = to the gods (dat. pl.)
• juhvati = they offer, sacrifice (3pl. pres. from √hu)
• ca = and
• pra = forth (prefix)
• pra juhvanti = they offer forth (3pl. pres. from pra-√hu) 		Therefore (tasmāt) [people] make oblations (juhvati) to the gods (devebhyaḥ) and (ca) also offer forth (pra juhvanti) [presents]. Explanation of ritual practice: people perform both huta (fire oblations) and prahuta (presenting offerings). This explains the dual nature of Vedic sacrifice. √hu - to sacrifice
Ritual practice: two types
Fire + presentation
atho āhur darśa-pūrṇamāsau iti • atho (atha + u) = but, moreover
• āhuḥ = they say (3pl. perf. from √ah/√brū)
• darśa = new moon (m. from √dṛś)
• pūrṇamāsa = full moon (m.)
• -au = dual ending
• iti = thus 		But (atho) some say (āhuḥ) these are the new moon (darśa) and full moon (pūrṇamāsau) [sacrifices]. Alternative interpretation: the two foods are the darśa (new moon) and pūrṇamāsa (full moon) sacrifices. These are major Vedic rituals performed monthly. darśa - new moon
pūrṇamāsa - full moon
√dṛś - to see
Monthly sacrifices
tasmān na iṣṭi-yājukaḥ syāt • tasmāt = therefore
• na = not
• iṣṭi = sacrifice, offering (f. from √yaj)
• yājuka = performer, sacrificer (agent noun from √yaj)
• syāt = should be (3sg. opt. from √as) 		Therefore (tasmāt) one should (syāt) not (na) be a performer of desire-motivated sacrifices (iṣṭi-yājukaḥ). Ethical teaching: avoid iṣṭi sacrifices motivated by selfish desires. These two foods for gods are pure offerings, not for personal gain. Optative syāt = obligation/recommendation. iṣṭi - sacrifice
√yaj - to sacrifice
√as (opt.) - should be
Avoid selfish rituals
MILK - THE FOOD FOR ANIMALS
'paśubhya ekaṃ prāyacchat' iti
tat payaḥ		 • paśubhyaḥ = to animals (dat. pl. m. from paśu)
• ekam = one (acc. n.)
• prāyacchat = gave (3sg. imperf. from pra-√yam/dā)
• tat = that
• payaḥ = milk (nom./acc. n. from payas) 		[Regarding] "One (ekam) he gave (prāyacchat) to animals (paśubhyaḥ)" - that (tat) is milk (payaḥ). Identification: the one food for animals (paśu) is milk (payas). This sustains both humans and animals in infancy. Central to Vedic cosmology. paśu - animal, cattle
payas - milk, fluid
pra-√dā - to give forth
Universal nourishment
payo hy eva agre
manuṣyāḥ ca paśavaḥ ca upajīvanti		 • payaḥ = milk (nom. n.)
• hy (hi) = for, indeed
• eva = exactly, indeed
• agre = in the beginning, at first (loc. from agra)
• manuṣyāḥ = humans (nom. pl. m.)
• ca = and
• paśavaḥ = animals (nom. pl. m.)
• upajīvanti = they live on, subsist on (3pl. pres. from upa-√jīv) 		For (hi) indeed (eva) in the beginning (agre) both humans (manuṣyāḥ) and (ca) animals (paśavaḥ) live on (upajīvanti) milk (payaḥ). Universal truth: milk is the first food (agre) for all mammals. Both manuṣya and paśu begin life sustained by payas. √jīv with upa- = "to live upon, subsist by". agra - beginning, front
manuṣya - human
upa-√jīv - to live on
First food of life
tasmāt kumāram jātam
ghṛtaṃ vai vā agre pratilehayanti
stanam vā anudhāpayanti		 • tasmāt = therefore
• kumāram = child, boy (acc. m.)
• jātam = born (acc. m. PPP from √jan)
• ghṛtam = ghee, clarified butter (acc. n.)
• vai = indeed, truly
• vā = or
• agre = at first
• pratilehayanti = they make lick (3pl. pres. caus. from prati-√lih)
• stanam = breast, nipple (acc. m.)
• anudhāpayanti = they make suckle (caus. from anu-√dhe) 		Therefore (tasmāt), the born (jātam) child (kumāram) is first (agre) made to lick (pratilehayanti) ghee (ghṛtam), or (vā) they are made to suckle (anudhāpayanti) the breast (stanam). Cultural practice: newborns (kumāra jāta) receive either ghee (ghṛta) or breast milk (stana) as first food. √lih = "to lick", √dhe = "to suck". This confirms milk's primacy. kumāra - child
ghṛta - ghee
√lih - to lick
√dhe - to suck
First feeding ritual
atha vatsam jātam āhur
atṛṇādaḥ iti		 • atha = now, then, and
• vatsam = calf (acc. m.)
• jātam = born (acc. m. PPP)
• āhuḥ = they say (3pl. perf.)
• atṛṇādaḥ = not eating grass (nom. m. compound: a-tṛṇa-ada)
• a = not (negative prefix)
• tṛṇa = grass, straw
• ada = eating (from √ad)
• iti = thus 		And (atha) of a calf (vatsam) that is born (jātam) they say (āhuḥ) "it does not yet eat (atṛṇādaḥ) grass (tṛṇa)". Parallel example: newborn calves (vatsa jāta) are called atṛṇāda "non-grass-eater" because they survive only on milk initially. Confirms milk's universality as first food. vatsa - calf
tṛṇa - grass
√ad - to eat
Before solid food
'tasmin sarvaṃ pratiṣṭhitam
yacca prāṇiti yacca na' iti
payasi hī idam sarvam pratiṣṭhitam
yacca prāṇiti yacca na		 • tasmin = in/on that (loc. n.)
• sarvam = all, everything (nom./acc. n.)
• pratiṣṭhitam = established, resting (PPP from prati-√sthā)
• yat = what, which (relative)
• ca = and
• prāṇiti = breathes, lives (3sg. pres. from √an with prāṇa)
• na = not
• payasi = in/on milk (loc. n.)
• hi = indeed
• idam = this 		[Regarding] "On it (tasmin) everything (sarvam) rests (pratiṣṭhitam), what (yat) breathes (prāṇiti) and (ca) what does not (na)" - indeed (hi) on milk (payasi) all (sarvam) this (idam) rests (pratiṣṭhitam), what (yat) breathes (prāṇiti) and (ca) what does not (na). Cosmic significance: ALL existence (sarvam) - both animate (prāṇiti "what breathes") and inanimate (na prāṇiti) - depends on milk. √sthā with prati- = "to stand upon, be established in". Milk as cosmic foundation. prati-√sthā - to be established
√an - to breathe
Animate vs inanimate
Milk = foundation
CONQUERING REPEATED DEATH
tad yad idam āhuḥ
saṃvatsaram payasā juhvat
apa punaḥ-mṛtyum jayati iti
na tathā vidyāt		 • tat = that, now
• yat = what, which
• idam = this
• āhuḥ = they say (3pl. perf.)
• saṃvatsaram = year (acc. m. from saṃvatsara)
• payasā = with milk (inst. n.)
• juhvat = offering (pres. part. from √hu)
• apa = away (prefix)
• punaḥ-mṛtyum = repeated death (acc. m. compound)
• jayati = conquers, wins (3sg. pres. from √ji)
• na = not
• tathā = thus, in that way
• vidyāt = should know (3sg. opt. from √vid) 		Now (tat) regarding what (yat) they say (āhuḥ) "By [one] offering (juhvat) milk (payasā) for a year (saṃvatsaram) one conquers (jayati) repeated death (punaḥ-mṛtyum)" - one should (vidyāt) not (na) understand it thus (tathā). Refutation of literal interpretation: offering milk sacrifices for a full saṃvatsara (year) doesn't literally conquer punaḥ-mṛtyu (re-death/rebirth) through duration alone. Optative vidyāt = "should/must know". Higher understanding needed. saṃvatsara - year
punaḥ-mṛtyu - repeated death
√ji - to conquer
√vid (opt.) - should know
Not literal duration
yat ahaḥ eva juhoti
tat ahaḥ punaḥ-mṛtyum apajayati
evam vidvān		 • yat = which (relative)
• ahaḥ = day (nom./acc. n. from ahan)
• eva = indeed, very
• juhoti = offers (3sg. pres. from √hu)
• tat = that
• punaḥ-mṛtyum = repeated death (acc. m.)
• apajayati = conquers, overcomes (3sg. pres. from apa-√ji)
• evam = thus, in this way
• vidvān = knowing, knower (nom. m. perf. part. from √vid) 		On whatever (yat) day (ahaḥ) one offers (juhoti), on that (tat) very (eva) day (ahaḥ) the knower (vidvān) conquers (apajayati) repeated death (punaḥ-mṛtyum). Correct understanding: conquest of punaḥ-mṛtyu happens immediately (yat ahaḥ = "on that very day") for the vidvān (knower/one who understands). Knowledge, not mere ritual duration, liberates. √ji with apa- = "to conquer away". ahan - day
apa-√ji - to conquer away
vidvān - knower (perf. part.)
Immediate liberation
Knowledge key
sarvaṃ hi devebhyaḥ anna-ādyam prayacchati • sarvam = all (nom./acc. n.)
• hi = for, indeed
• devebhyaḥ = to the gods (dat. pl. m.)
• annādyam (anna-ādyam) = edible food (acc. n. compound)
• anna = food
• ādya = to be eaten, edible (gerundive from √ad)
• prayacchati = offers, gives (3sg. pres. from pra-√yam/dā) 		For (hi) he offers (prayacchati) all (sarvam) edible food (annādyam) to the gods (devebhyaḥ). The knower offers ALL food (sarva anna) to the gods (devebhyaḥ). Every meal becomes an offering. Gerundive ādya = "to be eaten, edible". This transforms eating into sacrifice. ādya - edible (gerundive)
pra-√dā - to give forth
All eating = sacrifice
Constant offering
THE IMPERISHABLE PERSON AS CAUSE
'kasmāt tāni na kṣīyante
adyamānāni sarvadā' iti
puruṣo vā akṣitiḥ
sa hī idam annam punaḥ punaḥ janayate		 • kasmāt = why, from what (abl. interrogative)
• tāni = those, they (nom./acc. n. pl.)
• na = not
• kṣīyante = are exhausted, decay (3pl. pres. pass. from √kṣi)
• adyamānāni = being eaten (nom./acc. n. pl. pres. pass. part. from √ad)
• sarvadā = always (adv. sarva + dā)
• puruṣaḥ = person, Self (nom. m.)
• vā = indeed
• akṣitiḥ = imperishable, indestructible (f. from a-kṣiti)
• sa = he
• hi = for, indeed
• idam = this
• annam = food
• punaḥ punaḥ = again and again
• janayate = produces, generates (3sg. pres. caus. from √jan) 		[Regarding] "Why (kasmāt) are they (tāni) not (na) exhausted (kṣīyante) though always (sarvadā) being eaten (adyamānāni)?" - The person (puruṣaḥ) indeed (vā) is the imperishable (akṣitiḥ) [cause], for (hi) he (sa) produces (janayate) this (idam) food (annam) again and again (punaḥ punaḥ). Philosophical key: food never runs out because puruṣa (the cosmic Person/Self) is akṣiti (imperishable) and continuously regenerates (punaḥ punaḥ janayate) food through consciousness and action. √kṣi = "to decay, perish". The unchanging Self perpetually manifests as changing food. puruṣa - Person, Self
akṣiti - imperishable
√kṣi - to perish
√jan (caus.) - to produce
Infinite regeneration
'yo vai tām akṣitim veda' iti
puruṣo vā akṣitiḥ		 • yaḥ = who (nom. m. relative)
• vai = indeed, truly
• etām = this (acc. f. from idam)
• akṣitim = imperishability (acc. f.)
• veda = knows (3sg. perf. from √vid, used as present)
• puruṣaḥ = person, Self
• vā = indeed
• akṣitiḥ = imperishable (f. nom.) 		[Regarding] "He who (yaḥ) knows (veda) this (etām) imperishability (akṣitim)" - the person (puruṣaḥ) indeed (vā) is the imperishable (akṣitiḥ) [cause]. Reiteration: knowing (veda) the akṣiti (imperishability) means understanding that puruṣa IS the imperishable source. Perfect tense veda used as present = "knows" (completed knowledge existing now). Self-knowledge is key. √vid (perf.) - knows
Knowledge of Self
Imperishable nature
Identity realized
sa hī idam annam dhiyā dhiyā
janayate karmabhiḥ		 • sa = he
• hi = for, indeed
• idam = this
• annam = food
• dhiyā dhiyā = through thought after thought (inst. f. from dhī, repeated)
• janayate = produces (3sg. pres. caus.)
• karmabhiḥ = through/from actions (inst. pl. n. from karman) 		For (hi) he (sa) produces (janayate) this (idam) food (annam) through thought after thought (dhiyā dhiyā), through actions (karmabhiḥ). Mechanism of regeneration: puruṣa creates food through repeated dhī (thought/intelligence) and karman (actions). The repetition "dhiyā dhiyā" emphasizes continuous mental activity. Mind (dhī) + action (karman) = manifestation of food. √dhī = "to think, meditate". dhī - thought, intelligence
√dhī - to think
karman - action, deed
Mind + action = creation
Continuous process
yat hi etat na karma kuryāt
kṣīyeta ha		 • yat = if (conditional use of relative)
• hi = indeed
• etat = this
• na = not
• karma = action (acc. n.)
• kuryāt = were to do, should do (3sg. opt. from √kṛ)
• kṣīyeta = would be exhausted (3sg. opt. pass. from √kṣi)
• ha = indeed, certainly (emphatic particle) 		If (yat) he (etat) were not (na) to do (kuryāt) this action (karma), [the food] would indeed (ha) be exhausted (kṣīyeta). Counterfactual: without continued karma (action) by puruṣa, food would kṣīyeta (be depleted/exhausted). Optatives kuryāt + kṣīyeta express hypothetical condition. Action sustains existence. Cessation of conscious action = cessation of manifestation. √kṛ (opt.) - were to do
√kṣi (opt. pass.) - would be exhausted
Necessity of action
Counterfactual
EATING WITH PRATĪKA (THE MOUTH)
'so 'nnam atti pratīkena' iti
mukham pratīkam
mukhena ity etat		 • saḥ = he
• annam = food (acc. n.)
• atti = eats (3sg. pres. from √ad)
• pratīkena = with pratīka; facing (inst. n. from pratīka)
• mukham = mouth, face (nom./acc. n.)
• pratīkam = facing, pre-eminence (nom./acc. n.)
• mukhena = through/with the mouth (inst. n.)
• ity (iti) = thus
• etat = this 		[Regarding] "He (saḥ) eats (atti) food (annam) with pratīka (pratīkena)" - the mouth (mukham) is pratīka (pratīkam); this (etat) means "through the mouth (mukhena)". Etymological explanation: pratīka literally means "facing, appearance, pre-eminent part" but here means mukha (mouth/face). The Self eats through the mouth as instrument. Pratīka = prati (towards) + √ī (to go) + ka = "what goes towards/faces". The mouth faces food. pratīka - face, appearance, counterpart
mukha - mouth, face
√ad - to eat
Mouth = interface
Etymology explained
'sa devān apigacchati
sa ūrjam upajīvati' iti
praśaṃsā		 • sa = he
• devān = gods (acc. pl. m.)
• apigacchati = attains, goes to (3sg. pres. from api-√gam)
• ūrjam = vigor, strength, sap (acc. f. from ūrj)
• upajīvati = lives on, subsists on (3sg. pres. from upa-√jīv)
• iti = thus
• praśaṃsā = praise, eulogy (f. from pra-√śaṃs) 		[Regarding] "He (sa) attains (apigacchati) the gods (devān), he (sa) lives on (upajīvati) vigor (ūrjam)" - this is praise (praśaṃsā). Concluding eulogy (praśaṃsā): the knower who understands this teaching attains the gods (devān apigacchati) and lives sustained by ūrja (vigor/vital sap). √gam with api- = "to go to, attain, reach". √śaṃs with pra- = "to praise, recite". The commentary ends with praise formula. api-√gam - to attain
ūrj - vigor, strength, sap
upa-√jīv - to live on
praśaṃsā - eulogy
Concluding praise
BṚHADĀRAṆYAKA 1.5.3 - THE THREE FOODS FOR THE SELF
'trīṇy ātmane akuruta' iti
manaḥ vācam prāṇam
tāni ātmane akuruta		 • trīṇi = three (nom./acc. n. pl.)
• ātmane = for himself, for the Self (dat. m. from ātman)
• akuruta = made, did (3sg. imperf. Ātm. from √kṛ)
• iti = thus
• manaḥ = mind (nom./acc. n. from manas)
• vācam = speech (acc. f. from vāc)
• prāṇam = breath, life (acc. m. from prāṇa)
• tāni = those, these (nom./acc. n. pl.) 		[Regarding] "Three (trīṇi) he made (akuruta) for himself (ātmane)" - [these are] mind (manaḥ), speech (vācam), and breath (prāṇam); these (tāni) he made (akuruta) for himself (ātmane). The three "self-foods" (ātmane = "for the Self"): manas (mind), vāc (speech), prāṇa (breath). These are internal faculties, unlike external foods. Ātmanepada akuruta = reflexive "made for himself". The Self's own instruments of manifestation. ātman - self, soul
manas - mind (√man - to think)
vāc - speech (√vac - to speak)
prāṇa - breath (pra-√an - to breathe forth)
Three internal faculties
THE PRIMACY OF MIND
anyatra manā abhūvam na adarśam
anyatra manā abhūvam na aśrauṣam iti		 • anyatra = elsewhere, in another place (adv.)
• manāḥ = with mind (inst. n. from manas)
• abhūvam = I was (1sg. root aorist from √bhū)
• na = not
• adarśam = I saw (1sg. imperf. from √dṛś)
• na = not
• aśrauṣam = I heard (aorist from √śru)
• iti = thus 		"When my mind (manāḥ) was (abhūvam) elsewhere (anyatra), I did not (na) see (adarśam); when my mind (manāḥ) was (abhūvam) elsewhere (anyatra), I did not (na) hear (aśrauṣam)" - thus. Common experience proving mind's primacy: without mental attention (manāḥ), sense organs don't function. "Anyatra manāḥ" = "mind elsewhere" = inattention. Even though eyes/ears work physically, perception requires manas. Mind coordinates all sensing. anyatra - elsewhere
√bhū (aorist) - I was
√dṛś - to see
√śru - to hear
Mind = prerequisite for perception
manasā hy eva paśyati
manasā śṛṇoti		 • manasā = with/through the mind (inst. n.)
• hy (hi) = for, indeed
• eva = indeed, exactly
• paśyati = sees, perceives (3sg. pres. from √paś/dṛś)
• śṛṇoti = hears (3sg. pres. from √śru) 		For (hi) indeed (eva) one sees (paśyati) with the mind (manasā), one hears (śṛṇoti) with the mind (manasā). Philosophical principle: all perception (paśyati, śṛṇoti) is ultimately mental (manasā). Eyes and ears are mere instruments; manas is the true perceiver. Eva emphasizes exclusivity - ONLY through mind does perception occur. √paś/√dṛś - to see
√śru - to hear
Mind = true perceiver
Senses = instruments
MENTAL FUNCTIONS - ALL ARE MIND
kāmaḥ saṅkalpaḥ vicikitsā
śraddhā aśraddhā
dhṛtiḥ adhṛtiḥ
hrīḥ dhīḥ bhīḥ iti
etat sarvam manaḥ eva		 • kāmaḥ = desire (nom. m. from √kam)
• saṅkalpaḥ = resolve, intention (nom. m. from sam-√kḷp)
• vicikitsā = doubt (f. from vi-√cit intensive)
• śraddhā = faith (f. from śrat-√dhā)
• aśraddhā = lack of faith (f.)
• dhṛtiḥ = firmness (f. from √dhṛ)
• adhṛtiḥ = lack of firmness (f.)
• hrīḥ = shame, modesty (f. from √hrī)
• dhīḥ = intelligence (f. from √dhī)
• bhīḥ = fear (f. from √bhī)
• iti = thus
• etat = this
• sarvam = all
• manaḥ = mind
• eva = indeed, only 		Desire (kāmaḥ), resolve (saṅkalpaḥ), doubt (vicikitsā), faith (śraddhā), lack of faith (aśraddhā), firmness (dhṛtiḥ), lack of firmness (adhṛtiḥ), shame (hrīḥ), intelligence (dhīḥ), fear (bhīḥ) - all (sarvam) this (etat) is indeed (eva) just the mind (manaḥ). Comprehensive list of mental states/functions, all identified as manas itself. Includes: 1) kāma (desire), 2) saṅkalpa (will/resolve), 3) vicikitsā (doubt), 4) śraddhā (faith) and its opposite, 5) dhṛti (steadfastness) and its opposite, 6) hrī (shame/modesty), 7) dhī (wisdom/understanding), 8) bhī (fear). All psychological phenomena reduce to mind. Eva = "only/just" mind. √kam - to desire
sam-√kḷp - to resolve
vi-√cit - to doubt
√dhṛ - to hold
√hrī - to be ashamed
√dhī - to think
√bhī - to fear
All mental states = mind
tasmād api pṛṣṭhataḥ upaspṛṣṭaḥ
manasā vijānāti		 • tasmāt = therefore
• api = even, also
• pṛṣṭhataḥ = from behind (adv. from pṛṣṭha + -tas)
• upaspṛṣṭaḥ = touched, contacted (nom. m. PPP from upa-√spṛś)
• manasā = through the mind (inst. n.)
• vijānāti = perceives, knows distinctly (3sg. pres. from vi-√jñā) 		Therefore (tasmāt) even (api) when touched (upaspṛṣṭaḥ) from behind (pṛṣṭhataḥ), one perceives (vijānāti) it through the mind (manasā). Even tactile perception from pṛṣṭhataḥ (behind = unseen location) requires manas. Physical contact (upaspṛṣṭa) is processed by mind. √jñā with vi- = "to know distinctly, discern". Mind perceives even without visual confirmation. Touch needs mental awareness. pṛṣṭha - back, rear
upa-√spṛś - to touch
vi-√jñā - to perceive distinctly
Even touch needs mind
SPEECH - ALL SOUND IS SPEECH
yaḥ kaḥ ca śabdaḥ
vāk eva sā eṣā hi
antam āyattā
eṣā hi na		 • yaḥ = whatever, who (nom. m.)
• kaḥ = who, what (interrogative as indefinite)
• ca = and (= whatever, any)
• śabdaḥ = sound, word (nom. m. from √śabd)
• vāk = speech (nom. f.)
• eva = indeed, alone
• sā = that, she (nom. f.)
• eṣā = this (nom. f.)
• hi = for, indeed
• antam = end, goal (acc. n. from anta)
• āyattā = dependent on, aiming at (nom. f. PPP from ā-√yat)
• na = not 		Whatever (yaḥ kaḥ ca) sound (śabdaḥ) there is, that (sā) is indeed (eva) speech (vāk) alone, for (hi) it (eṣā) aims at (āyattā) an end (antam); it does not (na) [exist independently]. All śabda (sound/word) is fundamentally vāc (speech). Speech is purposive - āyattā "aiming at" anta (an end/goal). √yat with ā- = "to depend on, aim at, strive for". Speech is not random noise but intentional communication towards meaning. No sound exists independently (na) of communicative intent. √śabd - to make sound
vāc - speech, voice
anta - end, goal
ā-√yat - to aim at, depend on
Sound = purposive speech
PRĀṆA - THE FIVE VITAL AIRS
prāṇaḥ apānaḥ vyānaḥ
udānaḥ samānaḥ anaḥ iti
etat sarvam prāṇaḥ eva		 • prāṇaḥ = the upward/forward breath (nom. m. from pra-√an)
• apānaḥ = the downward breath (nom. m. from apa-√an)
• vyānaḥ = the diffused breath (nom. m. from vi-√an)
• udānaḥ = the ascending breath (nom. m. from ud-√an)
• samānaḥ = the equalizing breath (nom. m. from sam-√an)
• anaḥ = respiration, breathing (nom. m. from √an)
• iti = thus
• etat = this
• sarvam = all
• prāṇaḥ = breath, life-force
• eva = indeed, only 		Prāṇa (prāṇaḥ), apāna (apānaḥ), vyāna (vyānaḥ), udāna (udānaḥ), samāna (samānaḥ), and ana (anaḥ) - all (sarvam) this (etat) is indeed (eva) just breath (prāṇaḥ). The five vital airs (pañca-prāṇa) plus generic breath (ana): 1) prāṇa (forward/upward - chest/throat), 2) apāna (downward - lower body), 3) vyāna (diffused - throughout body), 4) udāna (ascending - head/upward), 5) samāna (equalizing - navel/digestion), 6) ana (generic breathing). All are manifestations of one life-force (prāṇa eva). √an = "to breathe, live". Each prefix modifies direction/function. pra-√an - forward breath
apa-√an - downward breath
vi-√an - pervasive breath
ud-√an - upward breath
sam-√an - equalizing breath
√an - to breathe
Five vital airs
THE SELF MADE OF THREE
etat-mayaḥ vā ayam ātmā
vāṅ-mayaḥ manaḥ-mayaḥ
prāṇa-mayaḥ		 • etat-mayaḥ = made of these, consisting of these (nom. m. compound)
• vā = indeed
• ayam = this (nom. m. from idam)
• ātmā = Self, soul (nom. m.)
• vāṅ-mayaḥ (vāk-mayaḥ) = made of speech (nom. m.)
• manaḥ-mayaḥ = made of mind (nom. m. compound manas-maya)
• prāṇa-mayaḥ = made of breath (nom. m.)
• -maya = made of, consisting of (suffix from √mā - to measure, form) 		This (ayam) Self (ātmā) indeed (vā) is made of these (etat-mayaḥ) [three], made of speech (vāṅ-mayaḥ), made of mind (manaḥ-mayaḥ), made of breath (prāṇa-mayaḥ). Concluding identification: the ātman (Self) consists of (maya) the three internal faculties: vāc (speech), manas (mind), prāṇa (breath). These three "foods made for himself" (1.5.3 opening) constitute the Self's manifestation. Suffix -maya = "consisting of, formed by". The Self IS these three, just as it IS the seven foods. Upaniṣadic identity formula. ātman - Self, soul
-maya - made of, consisting of
√mā - to measure, form
Self = mind + speech + breath
Complete identity

Śvetāśvatara Upaniṣad - Chapter 1

Verses 1.1-12 - Philosophical Inquiry into Brahman

Sanskrit Text Word-by-Word Analysis Literal Translation Grammar Notes Key Terms
VERSE 1.1 - OPENING QUESTIONS ON BRAHMAN
oṃ • oṃ = sacred syllable Om (oṃ) Opens with sacred syllable Om, the primordial sound representing Brahman. oṃ = sacred syllable
praṇava = Om
kiṃkāraṇaṃ brahma
kutaḥ sma jātā
jīvāmaḥ kena		 • kim-kāraṇam = what-cause (nom. sg. n.)
• brahma = Brahman (nom. sg. n.)
• kutaḥ = from where? whence? (adv.)
• sma = particle (past emphasis)
• jātāḥ = born (nom. pl. m. PPP from √jan)
• jīvāmaḥ = we live (1st pl. pres. from √jīv)
• kena = by what? (instr. sg. n. interr.) 		What (kim) is the cause (kāraṇam), [what is] Brahman (brahma)? From where (kutaḥ) were we born (jātāḥ)? By what (kena) do we live (jīvāmaḥ)? Three foundational questions: (1) What is the ultimate cause/Brahman? (2) What is our origin? (3) What sustains us? Particle sma adds past emphasis. Interrogatives kim, kutaḥ, kena probe cause, origin, means. kāraṇa = cause
√jan = to be born
√jīv = to live
Three questions
kva ca saṃpratiṣṭhāḥ • kva = where? (adv.)
• ca = and
• saṃpratiṣṭhāḥ = established, resting (nom. pl. m. from sam-prati-√sthā) 		And (ca) where (kva) are [we] established (saṃpratiṣṭhāḥ)? Fourth question: our foundation/support. Compound sam-prati-sthā = "well-established, firmly based". Where do we rest/stand? What is our ontological ground? sam-prati-√sthā = to be established
Question 4
adhiṣṭhitāḥ kena
sukhetareṣu vartāmahe		 • adhiṣṭhitāḥ = ruled over, governed (nom. pl. m. PPP from adhi-√sthā)
• kena = by what/whom? (instr. sg. n./m. interr.)
• sukha-itareṣu = in pleasure and its opposite (loc. pl. n.)
• vartāmahe = we exist, abide (1st pl. mid. pres. from √vṛt) 		Governed (adhiṣṭhitāḥ) by what (kena) do we exist (vartāmahe) in pleasure (sukha) and its opposite (itareṣu) [pain]? Fifth question: who governs our experience of opposites? PPP adhiṣṭhita = "presided over, ruled". Compound sukha-itara = "pleasure-and-other" = pleasure and pain. Middle voice vartāmahe = "we revolve/exist" (from √vṛt "to turn"). What power rules our existence in duality? adhi-√sthā = to preside over
itara = other, opposite
√vṛt = to turn, exist
Question 5
brahmavido vyavasthām • brahma-vidaḥ = O knowers of Brahman (voc. pl. m.)
• vyavasthām = determination, settled state (acc. sg. f.) 		O knowers (vidaḥ) of Brahman (brahma), [tell us] the determination (vyavasthām) [of these matters]. Vocative address to authorities. Compound brahma-vid = "Brahman-knower". Vyavasthā = determination, settled conclusion, definitive answer. Appeal to those who know to resolve these questions. brahma-vid = Brahman-knower
vyavasthā = determination
Vocative appeal
Full Verse Translation:

"What is the cause? What is Brahman? From where were we born? By what do we live? And where are we established? Governed by what do we exist in pleasure and pain? O knowers of Brahman, [tell us] the settled determination [of these matters]."
VERSE 1.2 - ANALYSIS OF PROPOSED CAUSES
kālaḥ svabhāvo niyatiḥ
yadṛcchā		 • kālaḥ = time (nom. sg. m.)
• svabhāvaḥ = inherent nature (nom. sg. m.)
• niyatiḥ = necessity, fate (nom. sg. f.)
• yadṛcchā = chance, accident (nom. sg. f.) 		Time (kālaḥ), inherent nature (svabhāvaḥ), necessity (niyatiḥ), chance (yadṛcchā)... Lists rival philosophical theories of causation. Each represents a different school: Time (Kālavāda), Nature (Svabhāvavāda), Fate (Niyativāda), Chance (Yadṛcchāvāda). kāla = time
svabhāva = own-nature
niyati = necessity
yadṛcchā = chance
bhūtāni yoniḥ puruṣa iti • bhūtāni = elements (nom. pl. n.)
• yoniḥ = womb, source (nom. sg. f.)
• puruṣaḥ = person, spirit (nom. sg. m.)
• iti = thus (quotative) 		...elements (bhūtāni), the womb (yoniḥ) [Prakṛti], the person (puruṣaḥ) - thus [say some]. More theories: Bhūtavāda (elements), Yoni (Sāṃkhya's Prakṛti/material cause), Puruṣa (conscious principle). The 'iti' marks these as views to be examined. bhūta = element
yoni = womb, source
puruṣa = person, spirit
Six theories listed
cintyam etad api ca
ātmasaṃyogānanda-
hetutve		 • cintyam = to be thought about (gerundive from √cit)
• etat = this (nom. sg. n.)
• api ca = moreover, also
• ātma-saṃyoga = conjunction with the Self
• ānanda-hetutve = in being the cause of bliss (loc. sg.) 		Moreover (api ca), this (etat) should be contemplated (cintyam): [these] in being the cause (hetutve) of the bliss (ānanda) that comes from conjunction (saṃyoga) with the Self (ātma). Gerundive cintyam = "must be thought about" (obligation). Question: can these theories explain spiritual bliss (ānanda) from Self-realization? Locative absolute construction. √cit = to think, perceive

ānanda = bliss

VERSE 1.3 - YOGIC VISION OF THE DIVINE POWER
te dhyānayogānugatā apaśyan
devātmaśaktiṃ svaguṇair nigūḍhām		 • te = they (nom. pl. m.)
• dhyāna-yoga-anugatāḥ = devoted to meditation-yoga (nom. pl. m. PPP from anu-√gam)
• apaśyan = they saw, perceived (3rd pl. impf. from √paś)
• deva-ātma-śaktim = the divine Self-power (acc. sg. f.)
• sva-guṇaiḥ = by its own qualities (instr. pl. m.)
• nigūḍhām = hidden, concealed (acc. sg. f. PPP from ni-√guh) 		They (te), devoted to (anugatāḥ) the yoga (yoga) of meditation (dhyāna), saw (apaśyan) the divine (deva) Self-power (ātmaśaktim) hidden (nigūḍhām) by its own (sva) qualities (guṇaiḥ). First half: yogins as seers. PPP anugata from anu-√gam = "devoted to, following". Compound dhyāna-yoga = meditative practice. Imperfect apaśyan = completed vision. Object: deva-ātma-śakti = divine Self-power (God's Śakti). PPP nigūḍhā = concealed by its own guṇas (qualities/modes of prakṛti). Instrumental svaguṇaiḥ = means of concealment. dhyāna-yoga = meditation practice
√paś = to see, perceive
deva-ātma-śakti = divine Self-power
guṇa = quality, mode
ni-√guh = to conceal
yaḥ kāraṇāni nikhilāni tāni
kālātmayuktāny adhitiṣṭhaty ekaḥ		 • yaḥ = who (nom. sg. m. rel. pron.)
• kāraṇāni = causes (acc. pl. n.)
• nikhilāni = all, entire (acc. pl. n.)
• tāni = those (acc. pl. n. demons.)
• kāla-ātma-yuktāni = united with time and self (acc. pl. n.)
• adhitiṣṭhati = rules over, presides (3rd sg. pres. from adhi-√sthā)
• ekaḥ = the One (nom. sg. m.) 		[The divine power of] the One (ekaḥ) who (yaḥ) rules over (adhitiṣṭhati) all (nikhilāni) those (tāni) causes (kāraṇāni) united (yuktāni) with time (kāla) and self (ātma). Second half: relative clause describing the Supreme One. Verb adhi-√sthā = "to stand over, preside, govern". Nikhila = all, entire (comprehensive). Demonstrative tāni refers to causes from verse 1.2 (time, nature, fate, etc.). Compound kāla-ātma-yukta = "united/connected with time-and-self" - all temporal and conscious causes. Eka = the singular divine principle that transcends and rules all multiplicity. adhi-√sthā = to rule over, preside
nikhila = all, entire
kāla-ātma-yukta = time-self-united
eka = One, singular
Supreme ruler
Full Verse Translation:

"Those devoted to the yoga of meditation saw the divine Self-power hidden by its own qualities—[the power] of the One who alone rules over all those causes united with time and self."
VERSE 1.6 - THE SWAN SOUL IN BRAHMAN'S WHEEL
sarvājīve sarvasaṃsthe bṛhante
tasmin haṃso bhrāmyate brahmacakre		 • sarva-ājīve = life of all (loc. sg. m.)
• sarva-saṃsthe = support of all (loc. sg. m.)
• bṛhante = vast, great (loc. sg. m.)
• tasmin = in that (loc. sg. m.)
• haṃsaḥ = swan, soul (nom. sg. m.)
• bhrāmyate = wanders (3rd sg. pres. pass. from √bhram)
• brahma-cakre = wheel of Brahman (loc. sg. n.) 		In that (tasmin) vast (bṛhante) [wheel] which is the life of all (sarvājīve), the support of all (sarvasaṃsthe)—in that wheel of Brahman (brahmacakre) the swan (haṃsaḥ) wanders (bhrāmyate). The haṃsa (swan) is a metaphor for the individual soul (jīvātman). The locative compounds describe the brahma-cakra (wheel of Brahman/universe). Passive voice bhrāmyate suggests the soul's involuntary wandering in saṃsāra. haṃsa = swan (soul metaphor)
brahma-cakra = wheel of Brahman
√bhram = to wander
bṛhat = vast, great
pṛthag ātmānaṃ preritāraṃ ca matvā
juṣṭas tatas tenāmṛtatvam eti		 • pṛthak = separately, differently (adv.)
• ātmānam = self (acc. sg. m.)
• preritāram = mover, impeller (acc. sg. m. from pra-√īr)
• ca = and
• matvā = thinking, having understood (abs. from √man)
• juṣṭaḥ = favored, pleased (nom. sg. m. PPP from √juṣ)
• tataḥ = then, from that (adv.)
• tena = by Him (instr. sg. m.)
• amṛtatvam = immortality (acc. sg. n.)
• eti = goes (3rd sg. pres. from √i) 		Having understood (matvā) the self (ātmānam) and (ca) the mover (preritāram) as separate (pṛthak)—[when] favored (juṣṭaḥ) by Him (tena), then (tataḥ) [the soul] goes (eti) to immortality (amṛtatvam). Second half: path to liberation. Absolutive matvā = "having understood/thought". Pṛthak = separately (initially seeing duality between self and God). PPP juṣṭa from √juṣ = "favored, graced, blessed". When the soul, having first seen itself as separate from the divine mover/controller, is then blessed by Him, it attains amṛtatva (immortality/liberation). Instrumental tena = means of grace. pṛthak = separate, different
preritṛ = mover, impeller
√juṣ = to favor, bless
amṛtatva = immortality
Absolutive = matvā
Full Verse Translation:

"In that vast [wheel], the life of all, the support of all, in that wheel of Brahman the swan [soul] wanders. Having understood the self and the mover as separate, [when] favored by Him, then [the soul] goes to immortality."
VERSE 1.7 - THE SUPREME BRAHMAN
udgītam etat paramaṃ tu brahma
tasmiṃs trayaṃ supratiṣṭhākṣaraṃ ca		 • udgītam = sung, chanted (nom. sg. n. PPP from ud-√gai)
• etat = this (nom. sg. n.)
• paramam = supreme, highest (nom. sg. n.)
• tu = but, indeed
• brahma = Brahman (nom. sg. n.)
• tasmin = in it (loc. sg. n.)
• trayam = triad, three (nom. sg. n.)
• su-pratiṣṭhā = well-established
• akṣaram = imperishable (nom. sg. n.) 		This (etat) is sung (udgītam) as the supreme (paramam) Brahman (brahma); in it (tasmin) [is] the triad (trayam), well-established (supratiṣṭhā) and imperishable (akṣaram). Udgīta refers to the sacred Vedic chant. The trayam (triad) refers to: enjoyer, enjoyed, and impeller (or knower-known-knowledge). Compound su-pratiṣṭhā = "well-established". Akṣara = "imperishable syllable/reality". udgīta = sacred chant
parama = supreme
trayam = triad
akṣara = imperishable
pratiṣṭhā = established
atrāntaraṃ brahmavido viditvā
līnā brahmaṇi tatparā yonimuktāḥ		 • atra = here (adv.)
• antaram = difference, interior (acc. sg. n.)
• brahma-vidaḥ = Brahman-knowers (nom. pl. m.)
• viditvā = having known (abs. from √vid)
• līnāḥ = absorbed, dissolved (nom. pl. m. PPP from √lī)
• brahmaṇi = in Brahman (loc. sg. n.)
• tat-parāḥ = intent on That (nom. pl. m.)
• yoni-muktāḥ = freed from rebirth (nom. pl. m.) 		Having known (viditvā) the distinction (antaram) here (atra), the knowers of Brahman (brahmavidaḥ), absorbed (līnāḥ) in Brahman (brahmaṇi), intent on That (tatparāḥ), are freed from rebirth (yonimuktāḥ). Antara = "distinction/difference" between the triad and Brahman. Absolutive viditvā shows prior knowledge. Līnāḥ indicates complete absorption/dissolution. Yoni-mukta compound = "freed from the womb" (rebirth). antara = difference
√lī = to be absorbed
tat-para = devoted to That
yoni-mukta = freed from rebirth
VERSE 1.8 - THE LORD AND THE BOUND SOUL
saṃyuktam etat kṣaram akṣaraṃ ca
vyaktāvyaktaṃ bharate viśvam īśaḥ		 • saṃyuktam = united, joined (acc. sg. n. PPP from sam-√yuj)
• etat = this (acc. sg. n.)
• kṣaram = perishable (acc. sg. n.)
• akṣaram = imperishable (acc. sg. n.)
• ca = and
• vyakta-avyaktam = manifest-unmanifest (acc. sg. n. dvandva)
• bharate = supports (3rd sg. pres. Ātm. from √bhṛ)
• viśvam = universe (acc. sg. n.)
• īśaḥ = Lord (nom. sg. m.) 		The Lord (īśaḥ) supports (bharate) this (etat) united (saṃyuktam) perishable (kṣaram) and (ca) imperishable (akṣaram), manifest-unmanifest (vyaktāvyaktam) universe (viśvam). Dvandva compounds showing paired opposites: kṣara-akṣara (perishable-imperishable), vyakta-avyakta (manifest-unmanifest). Bharate (Ātmanepada) suggests the Lord's self-sustained support. The universe includes both changing and unchanging aspects. kṣara = perishable
akṣara = imperishable
vyakta = manifest
avyakta = unmanifest
√bhṛ = to support
anīśaś cātmā badhyate bhoktṛbhāvāj
jñātvā devaṃ mucyate sarvapāśaiḥ		 • anīśaḥ = powerless, not-lord (nom. sg. m.)
• ca = and
• ātmā = soul, self (nom. sg. m.)
• badhyate = is bound (3rd sg. pres. pass. from √bandh)
• bhoktṛ-bhāvāt = due to enjoyer-nature (abl. sg. m.)
• jñātvā = having known (abs. from √jñā)
• devam = God (acc. sg. m.)
• mucyate = is freed (3rd sg. pres. pass. from √muc)
• sarva-pāśaiḥ = from all bonds (inst. pl. m.) 		And (ca) the powerless (anīśaḥ) soul (ātmā) is bound (badhyate) due to (bhāvāt) its enjoyer-nature (bhoktṛ); having known (jñātvā) God (devam), it is freed (mucyate) from all (sarva) bonds (pāśaiḥ). Contrasts īśa (Lord) with anīśa (powerless soul). Passive verbs: badhyate (is bound), mucyate (is freed). Ablative bhāvāt shows cause: "due to being an enjoyer (bhoktṛ)". Absolutive jñātvā precedes liberation. Instrumental pāśaiḥ = "from bonds". anīśa = powerless
√bandh = to bind
bhoktṛ = enjoyer
√muc = to free
pāśa = bond, fetter
VERSE 1.9 - THE THREE UNBORN PRINCIPLES
jñājñau dvāv ajāv īśanīśāv
ajā hy ekā bhoktṛbhogārthayuktā		 • jña-ajñau = knowing-unknowing (nom. dual m. dvandva)
• dvau = two (nom. dual m.)
• ajau = unborn (nom. dual m.)
• īśa-anīśau = powerful-powerless (nom. dual m. dvandva)
• ajā = unborn (nom. sg. f.)
• hi = indeed
• ekā = one (nom. sg. f.)
• bhoktṛ-bhoga-artha-yuktā = connected with enjoyer-enjoyed-purpose (nom. sg. f.)
 Two (dvau) unborn ones (ajau)—knowing and unknowing (jñājñau), powerful and powerless (īśanīśau); and (hi) one (ekā) unborn (ajā) [prakṛti] connected (yuktā) with enjoyer (bhoktṛ), enjoyed (bhoga), and purpose (artha). Three unborn principles: (1) jña-ajña dvandva = jīva (knowing) and īśvara (unknowing of limitation) or puruṣa in bondage/freedom, (2) ajā ekā = prakṛti (feminine, one), (3) implied ātman. Complex compound bhoktṛ-bhoga-artha shows the material nature serving experience. jña = knowing
ajña = unknowing
ajā = unborn (f. = prakṛti)
bhoktṛ = enjoyer
bhoga = enjoyed
Dual compounds
anantaś cātmā viśvarūpo hy akartā
trayaṃ yadā vindate brahmam etat		 • anantaḥ = infinite (nom. sg. m.)
• ca = and
• ātmā = Self (nom. sg. m.)
• viśva-rūpaḥ = universal form (nom. sg. m. Bahuvrīhi)
• hi = indeed
• akartā = non-doer (nom. sg. m.)
• trayam = three (acc. sg. n.)
• yadā = when
• vindate = finds (3rd sg. pres. Ātm. from √vid)
• brahma = Brahman (nom. sg. n.)
• etat = this (nom. sg. n.) 		And (ca) the infinite (anantaḥ) Self (ātmā), of universal form (viśvarūpaḥ), indeed (hi) the non-doer (akartā)—when (yadā) one finds (vindate) [these] three (trayam), this (etat) is Brahman (brahma). The ātman is characterized by three qualities: ananta (infinite), viśva-rūpa (all-forms), akartā (non-agent). When the seeker comprehends (vindate) all three principles (trayam), this realization constitutes knowing Brahman. Ātmanepada vindate emphasizes personal realization. ananta = infinite
viśva-rūpa = universal form
akartṛ = non-doer
trayam = three
√vid = to find, know
VERSE 1.10 - PROGRESSIVE LIBERATION
kṣaraṃ pradhānam amṛtākṣaraṃ haraḥ
kṣarātmānāv īśate deva ekaḥ		 • kṣaram = perishable (nom. sg. n.)
• pradhānam = primary matter, prakṛti (nom. sg. n.)
• amṛta-akṣaram = immortal-imperishable (nom. sg. m.)
• haraḥ = Hara, Śiva (nom. sg. m.)
• kṣara-ātmānau = perishable and soul (acc. dual m.)
• īśate = rules (3rd sg. pres. Ātm. from √īś)
• devaḥ = God (nom. sg. m.)
• ekaḥ = one (nom. sg. m.) 		Matter (pradhānam) is perishable (kṣaram); Hara (haraḥ) is immortal-imperishable (amṛtākṣaram); the one (ekaḥ) God (devaḥ) rules (īśate) over the perishable and the soul (kṣarātmānau). Pradhāna = Sāṃkhya term for primordial matter/prakṛti. Hara = name of Śiva ("the destroyer/taker away"). Dual kṣarātmānau = "the perishable and the soul". Īśate (Ātmanepada) emphasizes the Lord's inherent sovereignty over both matter and individual souls. pradhāna = primary matter
hara = Śiva, destroyer
amṛta = immortal
√īś = to rule
Dual = two principles
tasyābhidhyānād yojanāt tattvabhāvād
bhūyaś cānte viśvamāyānivṛttiḥ		 • tasya = His (gen. sg. m.)
• abhidhyānāt = from meditation (abl. sg. n. from abhi-√dhyai)
• yojanāt = from union (abl. sg. n. from √yuj)
• tattva-bhāvāt = from reality-state (abl. sg. m.)
• bhūyaḥ = progressively, further (adv.)
• ca = and
• ante = at the end (loc. sg. m.)
• viśva-māyā-nivṛttiḥ = cessation of universal illusion (nom. sg. f.) 		From meditation (abhidhyānāt) on Him (tasya), from union (yojanāt), from reality-state (tattvabhāvāt), progressively (bhūyaḥ) and (ca) at the end (ante)—cessation (nivṛttiḥ) of universal illusion (viśvamāyā). Three ablatives showing progressive stages: abhidhyānāt (from meditation), yojanāt (from yoga/union), tattvabhāvāt (from abiding in reality). Bhūyaḥ = "increasingly, further". Result: viśva-māyā-nivṛtti = complete cessation of cosmic illusion. Ante = "ultimately, at the end". abhidhyāna = meditation
yojana = union, yoga
tattva-bhāva = reality-state
māyā = illusion

VERSE 1.11 - THREE STAGES OF LIBERATION
jñātvā devaṃ sarvapāśāpahāniḥ
kṣīṇaiḥ kleśair janmamṛtyuprahāṇiḥ		 • jñātvā = having known (abs. from √jñā)
• devam = God (acc. sg. m.)
• sarva-pāśa-apahāniḥ = removal of all bonds (nom. sg. f.)
• kṣīṇaiḥ = exhausted (inst. pl. m. PPP from √kṣi)
• kleśaiḥ = with afflictions (inst. pl. m.)
• janma-mṛtyu-prahāṇiḥ = cessation of birth-death (nom. sg. f.) 		Having known (jñātvā) God (devam)—removal (apahāniḥ) of all (sarva) bonds (pāśa); with afflictions (kleśaiḥ) exhausted (kṣīṇaiḥ)—cessation (prahāṇiḥ) of birth and death (janmamṛtyu). Two stages of liberation: (1) jñātvā devam leads to sarva-pāśa-apahāni (removal of all fetters), (2) kṣīṇaiḥ kleśaiḥ (instrumental absolute = "afflictions being exhausted") leads to janma-mṛtyu-prahāṇi (end of rebirth cycle). Kleśa = mental afflictions, defilements. √jñā = to know
apahāni = removal
√kṣi = to exhaust
kleśa = affliction
prahāṇi = cessation
tasyābhidhyānāt tṛtīyaṃ dehabhede
viśvaiśvaryaṃ kevala āptakāmaḥ		 • tasya = His (gen. sg. m.)
• abhidhyānāt = from meditation (abl. sg. n.)
• tṛtīyam = third (nom. sg. n.)
• deha-bhede = at dissolution of body (loc. sg. m.)
• viśva-aiśvaryam = universal lordship (nom. sg. n.)
• kevalaḥ = alone, absolute (nom. sg. m.)
• āpta-kāmaḥ = with desires fulfilled (nom. sg. m.) 		From meditation (abhidhyānāt) on Him (tasya), thirdly (tṛtīyam), at the dissolution (bhede) of the body (deha)—universal lordship (viśvaiśvaryam); alone (kevalaḥ), with desires fulfilled (āptakāmaḥ). Third stage: tṛtīya (third result). Deha-bhede (locative) = "at body-dissolution" (death). Result: viśva-aiśvarya = cosmic lordship, kevala = absolute/alone (kaivalya), āpta-kāma = all desires fulfilled. This describes videha-mukti (liberation after death) with divine powers. tṛtīya = third
deha-bheda = body-dissolution
aiśvarya = lordship
kevala = alone, absolute
āpta-kāma = fulfilled desires
VERSE 1.12 - THE ULTIMATE KNOWLEDGE
etaj jñeyaṃ nityam evātmasaṃsthaṃ
nātaḥ paraṃ veditavyaṃ hi kiṃcit		 • etat = this (nom. sg. n.)
• jñeyam = to be known (nom. sg. n. FPP from √jñā)
• nityam = eternally (adv.)
• eva = indeed
• ātma-saṃstham = existing in the Self (nom. sg. n.)
• na = not
• ataḥ = from this, beyond this (abl. adv.)
• param = other, beyond (nom. sg. n.)
• veditavyam = to be known (nom. sg. n. FPP from √vid)
• hi = indeed
• kiṃcit = anything (nom. sg. n. indefinite) 		This (etat) is to be known (jñeyam) as eternally (nityam) existing in the Self (ātmasaṃstham); beyond (param) this (ataḥ), indeed (hi), nothing (kiṃcit) else is to be known (veditavyam). Two FPPs (future passive participles/gerundives): jñeyam, veditavyam = "must be known". Ātma-saṃstha = "established in the Self". Negative statement: na ataḥ param kiṃcit veditavyam = "nothing beyond this needs to be known". This is the complete knowledge. jñeya = to be known
ātma-saṃstha = Self-established
veditavya = to be known
FPP = necessity
para = beyond
bhoktā bhogyaṃ preritāraṃ ca matvā
sarvaṃ proktaṃ trividhaṃ brahmam etat		 • bhoktā = enjoyer (nom. sg. m. agent noun from √bhuj)
• bhogyam = enjoyed (nom. sg. n. FPP from √bhuj)
• preritāram = impeller, mover (acc. sg. m. from pra-√īr)
• ca = and
• matvā = having understood (abs. from √man)
• sarvam = all (nom. sg. n.)
• proktam = declared (nom. sg. n. PPP from pra-√vac)
• trividham = threefold (nom. sg. n.)
• brahma = Brahman (nom. sg. n.)
• etat = this (nom. sg. n.) 		Having understood (matvā) the enjoyer (bhoktā), the enjoyed (bhogyam), and (ca) the impeller (preritāram)—all (sarvam) is declared (proktam): this (etat) threefold (trividham) Brahman (brahma). Summarizes the teaching with three principles: bhoktā (experiencer/puruṣa), bhogyam (experienced/prakṛti), preritāra (mover/īśvara). Absolutive matvā shows completion of understanding. Trividha = "threefold". Proktam = "fully declared/taught". This verse concludes the opening chapter's inquiry. bhoktṛ = enjoyer
bhogya = to be enjoyed
preritṛ = impeller
tri-vidha = threefold
√vac = to declare
VERSE 1.13 - FIRE HIDDEN IN WOOD METAPHOR
yathā yonigatasya mūrtir
na dṛśyate naiva ca liṅganāśaḥ		 • yathā = just as, even as (adv.)
• yoni-gatasya = of that which has gone into the womb/source (gen. sg. n.)
• mūrtiḥ = visible form, shape (nom. sg. f.)
• na = not
• dṛśyate = is seen (3rd sg. pres. pass. from √dṛś)
• na eva = nor indeed
• ca = and
• liṅga-nāśaḥ = destruction of the subtle form (nom. sg. m.) 		Just as (yathā) the visible form (mūrtiḥ) of that which has gone into its source (yonigatasya) is not (na) seen (dṛśyate), nor indeed (naiva) is there (ca) destruction of its subtle form (liṅganāśaḥ)... Fire metaphor begins. When fire returns to its source (wood), the visible form disappears but the subtle form (liṅga) is not destroyed. Passive verb dṛśyate from √dṛś. Compound yoni-gata = "gone into the womb/source". Liṅga-nāśa = destruction of the subtle/characteristic mark. yoni = womb, source
mūrti = visible form
liṅga = subtle form, mark
√dṛś = to see
sa bhūya evendra-
hanayonigṛhyas
tad vobhayaṃ vai
praṇavena dehe		 • saḥ = that, it (nom. sg. m.)
• bhūyas = again (adv.)
• eva = indeed
• indhana-yoni-gṛhyaḥ = grasped by its fuel-source (nom. sg. m.)
• tat = that (nom. sg. n.)
• vā = or
• ubhayam = both (nom. sg. n.)
• vai = indeed, truly
• praṇavena = by means of Om (instr. sg. m.)
• dehe = in the body (loc. sg. m.) 		...that (saḥ) is again (bhūyas) indeed (eva) grasped (gṛhyaḥ) by its fuel-source (indhanayoni); that (tat) both (ubhayam) [visible and subtle] truly (vai) [is realized] by means of Om (praṇavena) in the body (dehe). Fire emerges again (bhūyas) when grasped from its source through friction. Similarly, the Self (both gross and subtle aspects - ubhayam) is realized through praṇava (Om) practiced in the body. Compound indhana-yoni = "fuel-source". Instrumental praṇavena = "by means of Om". indhana = fuel
praṇava = Om
ubhaya = both

VERSE 1.14 - THE PRACTICE OF CHURNING
svadeham araṇiṃ kṛtvā
praṇavaṃ cottarāraṇim		 • sva-deham = one's own body (acc. sg. m.)
• araṇim = lower fire-stick (acc. sg. f.)

• praṇavam = Om (acc. sg. m.)
• ca = and

Meditation technique prescribed. Two fire-sticks (araṇi) needed for friction: body is lower stick, Om is upper stick. Absolutive kṛtvā shows sequential action. Compound uttara-araṇi = "upper churning stick". The body-Om combination generates spiritual fire. araṇi = fire-stick

Four parallel examples of hidden presence: oil pervades seeds, butter pervades milk, water pervades riverbeds, fire pervades wood. All use locative case for "in/within". That (tat) is the supreme (param) Brahman-teaching (brahmopaniṣat), that is the supreme Brahman-teaching (tad brahmopaniṣatparam). Triple compound: ātma-vidyā-tapas-mūla = "having Self-knowledge and austerity as root". The means are ātma-vidyā (Self-knowledge) and tapas (discipline). CHAPTER 2 - YOGA AND MEDITATION PRACTICE
VERSE 2.1 - SAVITṚ'S YOKING OF MIND
yuñjānaḥ prathamaṃ manas
tatvāya savitā dhiyaḥ		 • yuñjānaḥ = yoking, harnessing (pres. part. nom. sg. m. from √yuj)
• prathamam = first, foremost (acc. sg. n.)
• manaḥ = mind (acc. sg. n.)
• tatvāya = for the truth/that-ness (dat. sg. n.)
• savitā = the impeller, Savitṛ (sun deity) (nom. sg. m.)
• dhiyaḥ = thoughts, insights (acc. pl. f.) 		Savitṛ (savitā), yoking (yuñjānaḥ) first (prathamam) the mind (manaḥ) for truth (tatvāya), [yokes] the insights (dhiyaḥ)... Opens Chapter 2 with Vedic imagery. Savitṛ (solar deity of impulsion) yokes the mind and thoughts. Present participle yuñjāna from √yuj "to yoke" - key yoga root. Dative tatvāya = "for the purpose of truth". Adapted from Ṛg Veda 5.81.1. Sets up yoga practice as divine yoking. √yuj = to yoke (yoga root)
savitṛ = impeller, sun
manas = mind
dhī = insight, thought
tatva = truth, that-ness
agner jyotir nicāyya
pṛthivyā adhy ābharat		 • agneḥ = of fire (gen. sg. m.)
• jyotiḥ = light (acc. sg. n.)
• nicāyya = having gathered (abs. from ni-√ci)
• pṛthivyāḥ = from the earth (abl. sg. f.)
• adhi = from, upon
• ābharat = brought forth (3rd sg. impf. from ā-√bhṛ) 		...having gathered (nicāyya) the light (jyotiḥ) of fire (agneḥ), [Savitṛ] brought it forth (ābharat) from (adhi) the earth (pṛthivyāḥ). Absolutive nicāyya = "having gathered/collected". Savitṛ gathers inner fire/light from the earth (body/base). Imperfect ābharat indicates completed past action. Esoteric meaning: gathering the inner light of consciousness from the bodily base through yoga. Agni's light = consciousness/spiritual fire. agni = fire
jyotis = light
√ci = to gather, heap
√bhṛ = to carry, bring
pṛthivī = earth
VERSE 2.2 - YOKED MIND FOR HEAVEN
yuktena manasā vayaṃ
devasya savituḥ save
suvargeyāya śaktyā		 • yuktena = with yoked (instr. sg. n.)
• manasā = with mind (instr. sg. n.)
• vayam = we (nom. pl.)
• devasya = of the deity (gen. sg. m.)
• savituḥ = of Savitṛ (gen. sg. m.)
• save = under impulsion, instigation (loc. sg. m.)
• suvar-geyāya = for going to heaven (dat. sg. n.)
• śaktyā = with power, ability (instr. sg. f.) 		We (vayam), with yoked (yuktena) mind (manasā), under the impulsion (save) of the deity (devasya) Savitṛ (savituḥ), with power (śaktyā) for going to heaven (suvargeyāya)... Past participle yukta = "yoked" (from √yuj). Compound suvar-geya = "going to heaven/sun-world". Two instrumental means: yukta manasā (yoked mind) and śaktyā (spiritual power). Locative save = "under the impulsion of". The collective "we" indicates yogic community. Heaven = higher consciousness. yukta = yoked, joined
save = impulsion

• manasā = with mind (instr. sg. n.)
• devān = the gods (acc. pl. m.)
• svar = heaven, light (indecl.)
• yataḥ = whence, from where
• dhiyā = with thought (instr. sg. f.)
• divam = to heaven (acc. sg. m.) 		Having yoked (yuktvā) with mind (manasā) the gods (devān), whence (yataḥ) with thought (dhiyā) [going] to heaven (divam), to the light (svar)... Absolutive yuktvā = "having yoked". Yogin yokes the devān (inner divine faculties/senses) with mind. Two instrumental means: manasā (mind) and dhiyā (insight). Svar = heavenly light/realm. Movement from lower to higher consciousness indicated by "whence...to heaven". yuktvā = having yoked
deva = god, divine faculty

Future participle kariṣyatas = "those who will make/create". Savitṛ (divine impeller) pushes forward those yogins who will manifest the great light. The wise (viprāḥ) yoke (yuñjate) the mind (manaḥ) and also (uta) yoke the thoughts (dhiyaḥ) of the great (bṛhataḥ), all-knowing (vipaścitaḥ), inspired one (viprasya)... Middle voice yuñjate (they yoke for themselves). Viprāḥ (wise seers) yoke both manas (mind) and dhī (thought). Three epithets for the divine: vipra (inspired), bṛhat (great), vipaścit (all-knowing). The wise yoke their faculties to the supreme consciousness. Word-play: viprāḥ...viprasya. vipra = wise, inspired

Indeed (it) great (mahī) is the praise (pariṣṭutiḥ) of the deity (devasya) Savitṛ (savituḥ). Perfect dadhe = completed establishment. Compound vayuna-vit = "knower of paths" (knowledge of method). VERSE 2.5 - ANCIENT BRAHMAN AND IMMORTAL SONS

May the hymn (ślokaḥ) go forth (vi...etu) like (iva) [traveling] on a path (pathyā) of the sun (sūreḥ). First person yuje = "I yoke" (middle voice, reflexive yoga). Dual vām addresses two divine principles. Brahma pūrvyam = "ancient Brahman/sacred word" - primordial teaching. Instrumental namobhiḥ = means of connection. Optative etu = wish/prayer. Famous phrase: amṛtasya putrāḥ = "sons of immortality" (enlightened beings). Perfect tasthuḥ = stable establishment in divine realms. Relative clause: ye...tasthuḥ describes the qualified listeners. VERSE 2.6 - WHERE MIND ARISES
agnir yatrābhimathyate
vāyur yatrādhirudhyate
somo yatrātiricyate
tatra saṃjāyate manaḥ		 • agniḥ = fire (nom. sg. m.)
• yatra = where (adv.)
• abhimathyate = is churned (3rd sg. pres. pass. from abhi-√math)
• vāyuḥ = air, breath (nom. sg. m.)
• adhirudhyate = is restrained (3rd sg. pres. pass. from adhi-√rudh)
• somaḥ = soma (nom. sg. m.)
• atiricyate = overflows (3rd sg. pres. pass. from ati-√ric)
• tatra = there (adv.)
• saṃjāyate = is born, arises (3rd sg. pres. pass. from sam-√jan)
• manaḥ = mind (nom. sg. n.) 		Where (yatra) fire (agniḥ) is churned (abhimathyate), where breath (vāyuḥ) is restrained (adhirudhyate), where soma (somaḥ) overflows (atiricyate)—there (tatra) the mind (manaḥ) is born (saṃjāyate). Three-fold yogic process. Agni abhimathyate = fire churned (prāṇa awakened through practice). Vāyu adhirudhyate = breath restrained (prāṇāyāma). Soma atiricyate = nectar overflows (bliss arising). All passive verbs showing natural process. Result: saṃjāyate manaḥ = "mind is born/transformed" - higher mind emerges from yogic practice. Yatra...tatra = correlative (where...there). abhi-√math = to churn
adhi-√rudh = to restrain
ati-√ric = to overflow
soma = nectar, moon
sam-√jan = to be born together

The yogin should serve primordial truth through divine inspiration. prasava = impulsion, impulse

Aorist akṣipat suggests definitive non-destruction. yoni = womb, source

Yogic posture instruction. Tris-unnata = "thrice raised" (chest, neck, head or three-part torso). Sama śarīra = balanced body. Absolutive sthāpya = having established. VERSE 2.9 - BREATH CONTROL

kṣīne prāṇe nāsikayocchvasīta		 • prāṇān = breaths, vital airs (acc. pl. m.)
• prapīḍya = having compressed (abs. from pra-√pīḍ)
• iha = here, in this [body] (adv.)
• saḥ = he (nom. sg. m.)
• yukta-ceṣṭaḥ = one with controlled movements (nom. sg. m.)

• prāṇe = breath (loc. sg. m.)
• nāsikayā = through the nose (instr. sg. f.)
• ucchvasīta = should breathe out (3rd sg. opt. from ud-√śvas) 		Having compressed (prapīḍya) the breaths (prāṇān) here (iha), he (saḥ), one with controlled (yukta) movements (ceṣṭaḥ), when the breath (prāṇe) is diminished (kṣīne), should breathe out (ucchvasīta) through the nose (nāsikayā). Prāṇāyāma instruction. Absolutive prapīḍya = "having compressed/restrained". Compound yukta-ceṣṭa = "controlled in movement" (disciplined yogin). Locative absolute kṣīne prāṇe = "when breath diminishes". Optative ucchvasīta = should exhale. Nāsikayā = instrumental means. Precise breathing technique: compress, hold, exhale through nose when depleted. pra-√pīḍ = to compress

• vidvān = the wise one (nom. sg. m.)

• apramattaḥ = vigilant, unmindful (nom. sg. m.) 		Like (iva) a chariot (vāham) yoked (yuktam) with unruly (duṣṭa) horses (aśva), this (enam) mind (manaḥ) the wise one (vidvān), vigilant (apramattaḥ), should restrain (dhārayeta). Famous Upaniṣadic metaphor: mind = chariot with wild horses (senses). Triple compound: duṣṭa-aśva-yukta = "yoked with bad horses". Optative dhārayeta = should hold/restrain. Apramatta = vigilant, not careless (a-pramatta). The charioteer (buddhi/discrimination) must vigilantly control unruly horses (mind/senses). Echoes Kaṭha Upaniṣad 3.3-9. duṣṭa = unruly, wicked

VERSE 2.11 - PRELIMINARY VISIONS IN YOGA
nīhāradhūmārkānalānilānāṃ
khadyotavidyutsphaṭikāśaśīnām		 • nīhāra-dhūma-arka-anala-anilānām = of mist, smoke, sun, fire, wind (gen. pl. m.)
• khadyota-vidyut-sphaṭika-aśa-śīnām = of firefly, lightning, crystal, moon (gen. pl. m.) 		Of mist (nīhāra), smoke (dhūma), sun (arka), fire (anala), wind (anila), firefly (khadyota), lightning (vidyut), crystal (sphaṭika), moon (śaśin)... Two compounds listing nine preliminary visions in yoga. First group: nīhāra (mist), dhūma (smoke), arka (sun), anala (fire), anila (wind). Second group: khadyota (firefly), vidyut (lightning), sphaṭika (crystal), śaśin (moon). Genitive plural indicates possession of these forms. Progression from subtle to gross to luminous phenomena. nīhāra = mist
khadyota = firefly
vidyut = lightning
sphaṭika = crystal
Nine visions

• puraḥsarāṇi = preliminary, going before (nom. pl. n.)
• brahmaṇi = in Brahman (loc. sg. n.)
• abhivyakti-karāṇi = making manifest (nom. pl. n.)
• yoge = in yoga (loc. sg. m.) 		These (etāni) preliminary (puraḥsarāṇi) forms (rūpāṇi) making manifest (abhivyaktikarāṇi) Brahman (brahmaṇi) [arise] in yoga (yoge). Puraḥsara = "going before, preliminary" - these visions precede full realization. Compound abhivyakti-kara = "making manifestation" (revealing Brahman gradually). Locative brahmaṇi = "in relation to Brahman". Locative yoge = "in yoga [practice]". These are signs of progress, not final goal. Traditional yogic experiences documented. puraḥsara = preliminary

VERSE 2.12 - THE YOGA BODY
pṛthvyaptejo'nilakhe samutthite
pañcātmake yogaguṇe pravṛtte		 • pṛthvī-ap-tejas-anila-ākhe = earth, water, fire, wind, space (loc. sg. m.)
• samutthite = when arisen (loc. sg. abs. PPP from sam-ud-√sthā)
• pañca-ātmake = fivefold (loc. sg. m.)
• yoga-guṇe = quality/attribute of yoga (loc. sg. m.)
• pravṛtte = when manifested (loc. sg. abs. PPP from pra-√vṛt) 		When arisen (samutthite) [is] the fivefold (pañcātmake) [experience] of earth (pṛthvī), water (ap), fire (tejas), wind (anila), space (ākha), when manifested (pravṛtte) [is] the quality (guṇe) of yoga (yoga)... Five-fold compound of elements (pañca-mahābhūta): pṛthvī, ap, tejas, anila, ākāśa. Two locative absolutes: samutthite and pravṛtte = "when arisen...when manifested". Pañcātmaka = "having five as essence". Yoga-guṇa = yogic attribute/experience of elements. When five elements are experienced in yoga practice... pañca-mahābhūta = five great elements
sam-ud-√sthā = to arise
yoga-guṇa = yoga quality
LOC ABS = temporal clause
na tasya rogo na jarā na mṛtyuḥ

• tasya = of him, for him (gen. sg. m.)
• rogaḥ = disease (nom. sg. m.)
• jarā = old age (nom. sg. f.)
• mṛtyuḥ = death (nom. sg. m.)
• prāptasya = for one who has obtained (gen. sg. m. PPP from pra-√āp)
• yoga-agni-mayam = made of yoga-fire (acc. sg. n.)
• śarīram = body (acc. sg. n.) 		For him (tasya) [there is] not (na) disease (rogaḥ), not old age (jarā), not death (mṛtyuḥ), for one who has obtained (prāptasya) a body (śarīram) made of (mayam) yoga-fire (yogāgni). Triple negation: na roga, na jarā, na mṛtyu = freedom from disease, aging, death. Compound yoga-agni-maya = "made of yoga-fire" (transformed subtle body). PPP prāpta = "obtained, achieved". The yogin obtains an incorruptible subtle body (yoga-deha) free from normal limitations. Famous promise of yogic transformation. Genitive tasya shows possession/experience. roga = disease
jarā = old age
yoga-agni-maya = made of yoga-fire
Triple negation = complete freedom
Yoga-deha = yoga body
VERSE 2.13 - SIGNS OF YOGIC PROGRESS
laghutvam ārogyam alolupatvaṃ
varṇaprasādaḥ svarasauṣṭhavaṃ ca		 • laghutva = lightness (nom. sg. n.)
• ārogyam = health (nom. sg. n.)
• alolupatvam = non-greed, detachment (nom. sg. n.)
• varṇa-prasādaḥ = clarity of complexion (nom. sg. m.)
• svara-sauṣṭhavam = sweetness of voice (nom. sg. n.)
• ca = and 		Lightness (laghutva), health (ārogyam), detachment (alolupatvam), clarity (prasādaḥ) of complexion (varṇa), and (ca) sweetness (sauṣṭhavam) of voice (svara)... Five positive signs. Laghutvam (lightness - bodily and mental). Ārogya (health, freedom from disease). Alolupatva = a-lolupa-tva = "state of non-greed". Compound varṇa-prasāda = "complexion-clarity" (radiant skin). Compound svara-sauṣṭhava = "voice-sweetness" (melodious speech). Observable physical and psychological transformations. laghu = light
ārogya = health
a-lolupa = non-greedy
prasāda = clarity
sauṣṭhava = sweetness
gandhaḥ śubho mūtrapurīṣam alpaṃ
yogapravṛttiṃ prathamāṃ vadanti		 • gandhaḥ = smell, odor (nom. sg. m.)
• śubhaḥ = auspicious, pleasant (nom. sg. m.)
• mūtra-purīṣam = urine and feces (nom. sg. n.)
• alpam = little, minimal (nom. sg. n.)
• yoga-pravṛttim = commencement of yoga (acc. sg. f.)
• prathamām = first, initial (acc. sg. f.)
• vadanti = they say, declare (3rd pl. pres. from √vad) 		...pleasant (śubhaḥ) smell (gandhaḥ), minimal (alpam) urine and feces (mūtrapurīṣam)—[these] they say (vadanti) [are] the first (prathamām) manifestation (pravṛttim) of yoga (yoga). Two more signs: śubha gandha (pleasant body odor), alpa mūtra-purīṣa (minimal excretions). Compound yoga-pravṛtti = "yoga-manifestation/commencement". Prathama = "first, preliminary". Vadanti = traditional teaching ("they say" - authorities). Compound mūtra-purīṣa shows paired waste products. These eight signs indicate successful beginning of yogic transformation. Practical, observable criteria. gandha = smell, odor
alpa = little, minimal
pravṛtti = commencement
prathama = first
Eight signs total
VERSE 2.14 - THE MIRROR METAPHOR
yathaiva bimbaṃ mṛdayopaliptaṃ
tejomayaṃ bhrājate tat sudhāntam		 • yathā = just as (adv.)
• eva = indeed
• bimbam = mirror (nom. sg. n.)
• mṛdayā = with clay (instr. sg. f.)
• upaliptam = smeared, covered (nom. sg. n. PPP from upa-√lip)
• tejas-mayam = radiant, made of light (nom. sg. n.)
• bhrājate = shines (3rd sg. mid. pres. from √bhrāj)
• tat = that (nom. sg. n.)
• sudhāntam = well-cleaned (nom. sg. n.) 		Just as (yathā) indeed (eva) a mirror (bimbam) smeared (upaliptam) with clay (mṛdayā) shines (bhrājate) radiant (tejomayam) when (tat) well-cleaned (sudhāntam)... Simile begins: yathā...evam (as...so). Bimba = mirror/reflection. PPP upalipta = "smeared over" (obscured). Instrumental mṛdayā = means of covering. Compound tejas-maya = "made of light" (naturally radiant). Sudhānta = su-dhānta = "well cleaned". Middle voice bhrājate = shines (inherently). Mirror covered with clay → cleaned → shines. Metaphor for Self covered by impurities. bimba = mirror, reflection
upa-√lip = to smear
tejas-maya = made of light
su-dhānta = well-cleaned
Simile = mirror
tad vātmatattvaṃ prasamīkṣya dehī
ekaḥ kṛtārtho bhavate vītaśokaḥ		 • tat = that, thus (adv.)
• vā = or, indeed
• ātma-tattvam = reality of Self (acc. sg. n.)
• prasamīkṣya = having seen completely (abs. from pra-sam-√īkṣ)
• dehī = embodied one (nom. sg. m.)
• ekaḥ = one, alone (nom. sg. m.)
• kṛta-arthaḥ = one whose purpose is fulfilled (nom. sg. m.)
• bhavate = becomes (3rd sg. mid. pres. from √bhū)
• vīta-śokaḥ = free from sorrow (nom. sg. m.) 		...so (tat vā) the embodied one (dehī), having completely seen (prasamīkṣya) the reality (tattvam) of the Self (ātma), becomes (bhavate) one (ekaḥ), fulfilled in purpose (kṛtārthaḥ), free from sorrow (vītaśokaḥ). Application of simile. Absolutive prasamīkṣya from pra-sam-√īkṣ = "having completely perceived". Compound ātma-tattva = "Self-reality/truth". Dehī = embodied soul (still has body but transformed). Three results: (1) eka = unified/singular (non-dual), (2) kṛta-artha = fulfilled purpose (life's goal achieved), (3) vīta-śoka = "gone-sorrow" = sorrowless. Middle bhavate = becomes (natural transformation). Clean mirror = realized Self. pra-sam-√īkṣ = to see completely
kṛta-artha = fulfilled purpose
vīta-śoka = free from sorrow
dehī = embodied one
Three results
VERSE 2.15 - LAMP METAPHOR AND LIBERATION
yad ātmatattvena tu brahmatattvaṃ
dīpopameneha yuktaḥ prapaśyet		 • yat = when, if (temporal conj.)
• ātma-tattvena = by means of Self-reality (instr. sg. n.)
• tu = but, indeed
• brahma-tattvam = reality of Brahman (acc. sg. n.)
• dīpa-upamena = by lamp-metaphor (instr. sg. n.)
• iha = here, in this [body] (adv.)
• yuktaḥ = yoked, concentrated (nom. sg. m.)
• prapaśyet = one should see (3rd sg. opt. from pra-√paś) 		When (yat) indeed (tu) by means of (tattvena) the Self-reality (ātma) [one perceives] the Brahman-reality (brahmatattvaṃ), here (iha) by the lamp-metaphor (dīpopamena), the concentrated one (yuktaḥ) should see (prapaśyet)... Temporal clause with yat. Instrumental ātma-tattvena = "by means of Self-knowledge" (knowing microcosm). Object brahma-tattva = macrocosmic reality. Compound dīpa-upama = "lamp-simile". Yukta = concentrated yogin. Optative prapaśyet = prescription. Iha = in this very body. Method: know Self → know Brahman, like lamp illuminating (self-luminous consciousness). ātma-tattva = Self-reality
brahma-tattva = Brahman-reality
dīpa-upama = lamp-simile
yukta = concentrated
Microcosm→Macrocosm
ajaṃ dhruvaṃ sarvatatt vair viśuddhaṃ
jñātvā devaṃ mucyate sarvapāśaiḥ		 • ajam = unborn (acc. sg. m.)
• dhruvam = immovable, eternal (acc. sg. m.)
• sarva-tattvaiḥ = by all elements/realities (instr. pl. n.)
• viśuddham = completely pure (acc. sg. m.)
• jñātvā = having known (abs. from √jñā)
• devam = the deity, God (acc. sg. m.)
• mucyate = is freed (3rd sg. pass. pres. from √muc)
• sarva-pāśaiḥ = from all bonds (abl. pl. m.) 		...the unborn (ajam), eternal (dhruvam), completely pure (viśuddham) by all elements (sarvatatt vaiḥ) [God], having known (jñātvā) the deity (devam), one is freed (mucyate) from all (sarva) bonds (pāśaiḥ). Four epithets of God: (1) aja = "unborn" (eternal), (2) dhruva = "immovable" (unchanging), (3) sarva-tattva-viśuddha = "pure from all elements" (transcendent), (4) deva = divine. Absolutive jñātvā = causal "having known". Passive mucyate = liberation happens naturally upon knowledge. Ablative sarva-pāśaiḥ = "from all bonds" (complete freedom). Compound sarva-pāśa = all fetters (bondage). Knowledge → immediate liberation. aja = unborn
dhruva = eternal, immovable
viśuddha = completely pure
√muc = to free, liberate
pāśa = bond, fetter
VERSE 2.16 - THE ALL-FACING GOD
eṣa ha devaḥ pradiśo 'nu sarvāḥ
pūrvo ha jātaḥ sa u garbhe antaḥ		 • eṣaḥ = this (nom. sg. m.)
• ha = indeed (particle)
• devaḥ = deity, God (nom. sg. m.)
• pradiśaḥ = directions (acc. pl. f.)
• anu = along, throughout
• sarvāḥ = all (acc. pl. f.)
• pūrvaḥ = first, primordial (nom. sg. m.)
• jātaḥ = born (nom. sg. m. PPP from √jan)
• saḥ = he (nom. sg. m.)
• u = and, also (particle)
• garbhe = in the womb (loc. sg. m.)
• antaḥ = within (adv.) 		This (eṣaḥ) God (devaḥ) indeed (ha) [exists] throughout (anu) all (sarvāḥ) directions (pradiśaḥ); he (saḥ) was born (jātaḥ) first (pūrvaḥ), and (u) he [is] within (antaḥ) the womb (garbhe)... Particle ha = emphasis. Pradiśaḥ anu sarvāḥ = "along all directions" (omnipresent). Pūrva jāta = "first-born" (primordial). Paradox: first born yet unborn (aja from 2.15). Garbhe antaḥ = "within the womb" - immanent. God is both transcendent (all directions) and immanent (in womb/heart). Particle u adds emphasis. pradiś = direction
pūrva = first, primordial
garbha = womb, embryo
Transcendent & Immanent
sa eva jātaḥ sa janiṣyamānaḥ
pratyaṅ janās tiṣṭhati sarvatomukhaḥ		 • saḥ = he (nom. sg. m.)
• eva = indeed
• jātaḥ = born (nom. sg. m. PPP)
• janiṣyamāṇaḥ = about to be born (nom. sg. m. fut. pass. part.)
• pratyak = facing inward (adv.)
• janāḥ = people (voc. pl. m.)
• tiṣṭhati = stands (3rd sg. pres. from √sthā)
• sarvatas-mukhaḥ = all-faced, facing all directions (nom. sg. m.) 		...he (saḥ) himself (eva) [is already] born (jātaḥ), he [is] being born (janiṣyamāṇaḥ), O people (janāḥ), he stands (tiṣṭhati) facing inward (pratyak), facing all directions (sarvatomukhaḥ). Triple time: pūrva jāta (was born), jāta (is born), janiṣyamāṇa (will be born) = eternal present. Future passive participle janiṣyamāṇa = continuous becoming. Pratyak = "facing inward" (in the heart). Compound sarvatas-mukha = "all-directional-faced" (omnipresent). Vocative janāḥ = direct address. God eternally born, being born, to be born - beyond time yet in time. Famous verse on divine omnipresence. janiṣyamāṇa = about to be born
pratyak = inward-facing
sarvatas-mukha = all-faced
Eternal present
Omnipresence
VERSE 2.17 - FINAL SALUTATION
yo devo agnau yo apsu
yo viśvaṃ bhuvanam āviveśa		 • yaḥ = who (nom. sg. m.)
• devaḥ = deity (nom. sg. m.)
• agnau = in fire (loc. sg. m.)
• aḥsu = in waters (loc. pl. f.)
• viśvam = all, entire (acc. sg. n.)
• bhuvanam = world (acc. sg. n.)
• āviveśa = has entered (3rd sg. perf. from ā-√viś) 		Who (yaḥ) [is] the deity (devaḥ) in fire (agnau), who [is] in waters (apsu), who (yaḥ) has entered (āviveśa) the entire (viśvam) world (bhuvanam)... Relative clause begins: yaḥ (who). Anaphora: yaḥ...yaḥ...yaḥ (who...who...who). Locatives: agnau, apsu = God in elements. Perfect āviveśa from ā-√viś = "has entered/pervaded". Viśva bhuvana = entire universe. Progressive expansion: fire → waters → whole world → plants → trees (next line). ā-√viś = to enter, pervade
viśva-bhuvana = entire world
Anaphora = repetition
Progressive expansion
ya oṣadhīṣu yo vanaspatīṣu
tasmai devāya namo namaḥ		 • yaḥ = who (nom. sg. m.)
• oṣadhīṣu = in herbs, plants (loc. pl. f.)
• vanaspatīṣu = in forest trees (loc. pl. m.)
• tasmai = to that (dat. sg. m.)
• devāya = to the deity (dat. sg. m.)
• namaḥ = salutation (nom. sg. n.)
• [repeated] 		...who (yaḥ) [is] in herbs (oṣadhīṣu), who [is] in forest trees (vanaspatīṣu)—to that (tasmai) deity (devāya), salutation (namaḥ), salutation (namaḥ)! Continuation: yaḥ oṣadhīṣu, yaḥ vanaspatīṣu = in herbs, in trees. Relative-correlative: yaḥ...tasmai (who...to that one). Double dative: tasmai devāya = "to that deity". Namas repeated (epizeuxis) = emphatic salutation. Chapter 2 concludes with universal vision: God pervades fire, water, world, plants, trees - everything. Final double namaḥ = complete surrender. Beautiful hymnic conclusion combining yoga practice with devotion. oṣadhi = herb, plant
vanaspati = forest tree
namas = salutation
Relative-correlative
Epizeuxis = repetition
Universal pervader
